ARTICLE II. - OCCUPATION TAXES[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, adopted June 9, 2015, amended art. II in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former art. II, §§ 18-31—18-42, was entitled "Occupation Taxes and Regulatory Fees", and derived from: Code 1987, §§ 13-1, 13-3—13-10, 13-12 and 13-13; Ord. of Feb. 14, 1995, § 1; and Ord. No. 2011-01, § 1, adopted May 10, 2011. 
Charter reference— Occupation taxes and business license fees, § 6.12. 
State Law reference— Business and occupation taxes, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-5 et seq.; local taxes and fees, Ga. Const. art. IX, § IV, ¶ I. 

Sec. 18-31. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases shall, for the purposes of this chapter, have the following meaning: 
Administrative fee shall mean the fee charged to each person, partnership, corporation or other entity subject to the occupation tax that approximates the reasonable cost of handling, processing, and collecting the occupation tax. 
City means the City of Blackshear, Georgia. 
Employee is defined hereinafter as: 
(1)  Except as otherwise provided in paragraph (2) of this definition, "employee" means an individual whose work is performed under the direction and supervision of an employer who withholds FICA, federal income tax, or state income tax from such individual's compensation or whose employer issues to such individual for purposes of documenting compensation a form I.R.S. W-2 but not a form I.R.S. 1099. 
(2)  An individual who performs work under the direction and supervision of one business or practitioner in accordance with the terms of a contract or agreement with another business which recruits such individual is an employee of the business or practitioner that issues to such individual for purposes of documenting compensation a form I.R.S. W-2. 
(3)  With respect to the taxation of businesses or practitioners with no location or office in Georgia, "employees" may only include employees working substantially in Georgia. 
Location or office shall include any structure or vehicle where a business, profession, or occupation is conducted, but shall not include a temporary or construction work site which serves a single customer or project or vehicle or used for sales or delivery by a business of practitioner of a profession or occupation which has a location or office. The renter's or lessee's location which is the site of personal property which is rented or leased from another does not constitute a location or office for the real property's owner, lessor, or the agent of the owner or lessor, unless the real property's owner, lessor, or the agent of the owner or lessor, in addition to showing the property to prospective lessees or tenants and performing maintenance or repair of the property, otherwise conducts the business of renting or leasing the real property at such site or otherwise conducts any other business, profession or occupation at such site. 
Occupation tax means a tax levied for revenue purposes on persons, partnerships, corporations, or other entities for engaging in an occupation, profession, or business in the City of Blackshear, Georgia. 
Practitioners of professions and occupations does not include a practitioner who is an employee of a business, if the business pays an occupation tax. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 18-32. - Occupation tax levied; computation of full-time employees; occupation tax schedule; administrative fee; limitations; issuance of certificate; certificate to be displayed. 
(a)  An occupation tax based upon number of employees is levied upon a person, partnership, corporation or other entity if such person, partnership, corporation or other entity: 
(1)  Has one or more locations or offices within the corporate limits of the city; or 
(2)  Is an out-of-state businesses or practitioners with no location or office in the city but: 
a.  Has employees or agents engaging in substantial efforts to solicit business or serve customers or clients within the corporate limits of the city; or 
b.  Owns personal or real property that generates income and is located within the corporate limits of the city. 
(b)  The occupation tax is calculated and levied based on the number of employees of the person, partnership, corporation or other entity as computed on a full-time basis or full-time position equivalent basis, provided that for the purposes of this computation an employee who works 40 hours or more weekly shall be considered a full-time employee and that the average weekly hours of employees who work less than 40 hours weekly shall be added and such sum shall be divided by 40 to produce full-time position equivalents. 
(c)  The occupational tax is levied in accordance with the following schedule: 
0—1 Employees ..... $20.00 
Each additional employee ..... $15.00 
Provided, however, that the city shall not impose an occupational tax of more than $360.00 on any person, partnership, corporation or other entity, regardless of the number of employees. 
(d)  A non-prorated, nonrefundable administrative fee of $100.00 is assessed in connection with obtaining an occupation tax certificate or the annual renewal of such certificate. Such fee shall be paid in full at the time a person, partnership, corporation or other entity applies for such occupation tax certificate. 
(e)  The city shall not require the payment of more than one occupation tax for each location of a business operated by a person, partnership, corporation or other entity. 
(f)  A person, partnership, corporation or other entity that has locations in Georgia and is subject to occupation tax by more than one local government in Georgia shall only be subject to occupation tax by the City of Blackshear for the number of employees who are employed within the corporate limits of the city, provided that: 
(1)  This limitation shall only apply when the business or practitioner has provided to the city satisfactory proof of current payment of the occupation tax of the other local government(s); and 
(2)  If an employee works for the same business in more than one jurisdiction, the city or county in which the employee works the most in a calendar year may count the employee for occupation tax purposes. 
(g)  A person, partnership, corporation or other entity with no location or office in Georgia shall only be required to pay occupation tax to the local government in Georgia where the largest dollar volume of business is done or service is performed by such business or practitioner, provided that: 
(1)  This limitation shall only apply when the person, partnership, corporation or other entity has provided to the city satisfactory proof of as to the applicability of this subsection; and 
(2)  If a person, partnership, corporation or other entity with no location or office in Georgia provides to the city proof of payment of a local business or occupation tax in another state that purports to tax the business's or practitioner's sales or services in this state, then the person, partnership, corporation or other entity shall be exempt from this occupation tax. 
(h)  Real estate brokers shall be subject to occupation tax pursuant to this article only if they maintain a principal or branch office in the city. 
(i)  Upon a person, partnership, corporation or other entity's payment of the occupation tax and compliance with all other regulations hereunder, the city clerk shall issue an occupation tax certificate to such person, partnership, corporation or other entity. 
(j)  Every person, partnership, corporation or other entity subject to payment of the occupation tax shall display a current occupation tax certificate in a conspicuous place at the location for which the certificate was issued. If the person, partnership, corporation or other entity does not have a permanent location within the city, the occupation tax certificate shall be shown to the city clerk or any police officer upon request. Any person, partnership, corporation or other entity who fails to comply with this subsection shall be subject to the general penalties set forth under section 1-12 of chapter 1 of this Code. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-33. - Practitioners of professions and occupations. 
Practitioners of professions and occupations enumerated in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9(c) shall pay the occupation tax as set forth in section 18-32 above, or shall pay an occupation tax of $400.00 per practitioner. On the tax return for 2015 or such later time as the practitioner first commences business in the city, the practitioner shall elect either method of taxation. Such election shall be changed for subsequent calendar years only by a written request filed by the practitioner on or before February 1 of the year in which the election is to be changed. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-34. - Insurance companies and agents. 
Each insurance company doing business in the city shall pay an annual license fee and other taxes as set forth under article IV of chapter 18. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-35. - Exemptions. 
(a)  No occupation tax shall be levied on the following: 
(1)  Disabled veterans of any war or armed conflict in which any branch of the United States Armed Forces was involved, whether under United States command or otherwise; 
(2)  Blind persons; 
(3)  Veterans of peace-time service in the United States Armed Forces who has a physical disability which was incurred during that service; 
(4)  Any practitioner whose office is maintained by and who is employed in practice exclusively by the United States, the state, a municipality or county of the state, or instrumentality of the United States, the state, or a municipality or county of the state; 
(5)  Any state or local authority, nonprofit organization, or vendor acting pursuant to a contract with a tax-exempt agricultural fair; 
(6)  Real estate brokers, except at the principal or branch office of a real estate broker; 
(7)  Motor vehicles required to be registered with the public service commission; 
(8)  Those businesses regulated by the Georgia Public Service Commission; 
(9)  Those electrical service businesses organized under Chapter 3 of Title 46 of the Official Code of Georgia; 
(10)  Any farm operation for the production from or on the land of agricultural products, but not including any agribusiness; 
(11)  Nonprofit, agricultural product cooperative marketing associations pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 2-10-105; 
(12)  Motor common carriers pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 46-7-15; 
(13)  Persons purchasing guano, meats, meal, flour, bran, cottonseed, or cottonseed meal and hulls in carload lots for distribution among the purchasers for use and not sale pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-5-355; 
(14)  Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-5-356 for persons selling or introducing into the city agricultural products or livestock, including animal products, raised in this state when the sale and introduction are made by the producer of the product and the sale is made within 90 days of the introduction of the product into the city; 
(15)  Depository institutions pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93; or 
(16)  Any business on which the levy of such occupation tax is prohibited by the laws of the State of Georgia or the United States. 
(b)  The exemptions and limitations contained in this ordinance shall not be construed to repeal or otherwise affect in any way any franchise fees, business taxes or other fees or taxes otherwise allowed by law. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-36. - Evidence of state registration when required. 
Each person, partnership, corporation or other entity who is licensed under Title 43 of the Official Code of Georgia Annotated by the examining boards of the Secretary of State's Office shall provide evidence of proper and current state licensure before any city occupation tax certificate may be issued. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-37. - Evidence of qualification required if applicable. 
(a)  Any person, partnership, corporation or other entity required to obtain health permits, bonds, certificates of qualification, certificates of competency or any other regulatory matter shall first, before the issuance of an occupation tax certificate, show evidence of such qualification. 
(b)  Any person, partnership, corporation or other entity required to submit an annual application for continuance of the business shall do so before the registration is issued. 
(c)  The city shall not impose registration or other regulatory requirements on attorneys authorized to practice law by the State Bar of Georgia. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-38. - Filing returns; other information required or requested; confidentiality. 
(a)  On or before January 1st of each year, person, partnership, corporation or other entity subject to this occupation tax ordinance shall file with the city clerk, on a form approved by and available from the city, a signed return attesting to the number of employees of such person, partnership, corporation or other entity during the calendar year. 
(b)  A person, partnership, corporation or other entity doing business in the city shall submit to the city clerk or make available to the city, within 30 days or such longer time period as the city deems appropriate, such information as may be required or requested by the city to determine the applicability and amount of the occupation tax or to facilitate levying or collecting the occupation tax. 
(c)  Information provided by a person, partnership, corporation or other entity to the city for the purpose of determining the applicability and amount of the occupation tax, or levying or collecting the occupation tax, is exempt from disclosure under O.C.G.A. § 50-18-70 et seq. Such information may be provided to the governing authority of another local government for occupation tax purposes or pursuant to court order or for the purpose of collecting occupation tax or prosecution for failure or refusal to pay occupation tax. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-39. - Date due; penalty and interest. 
(a)  Any occupation tax and administrative fee due pursuant to this article shall be due and payable annually within 30 days of January 1st for the ensuing calendar year. Occupation taxes imposed on businesses commencing after January 1st will be due and payable immediately prior to the commencement of business. 
(b)  If a person, partnership, corporation or other entity commences business in the city on or after July 1st in any year, the occupation tax for the remaining portion of the year shall be 50 percent of the tax imposed for the entire year. The administrative fee shall not be pro-rated. 
(c)  Payment of an occupation tax or administrative fee shall not be required prior to the commencement of business for attorneys, nor shall it in any other manner act as a precondition on the practice of law. 
(d)  Any person, partnership, corporation or other entity subject to any occupation tax or administrative fee imposed by this article which is unpaid for 90 days after the date on which payment was due shall be subject to a penalty of ten percent of the tax or fee due, and interest at the rate of 1.5 percent per month. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-40. - Enforcement; violations. 
(a)  It is the duty of the city clerk to administer and enforce the provisions of this article, to perform all functions necessary to administer and enforce the ordinance codified in this article and to summon violators of this article to appear before the Municipal Court of the City of Blackshear. The city clerk may issue executions against persons, partnerships, corporations or other entities for taxes or fees that are due and owing; and any penalty or any interest imposed under this article. 
(b)  The city clerk shall issue executions against persons, partnerships, corporations or other entities for taxes or fees which are due and owing, penalties or interest. Such executions shall bear interest at the rate authorized by O.C.G.A. § 48-2-40 or, if such statute should be repealed or ruled invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, one percent per month. The lien shall cover the property of the person, partnership, corporation or other entity liable for payment of the delinquent occupation tax and become fixed as of the date and time the occupation tax became delinquent. The execution shall be levied by the city clerk upon property of the delinquent tax or fee payer located in the city and sufficient property shall be advertised and sold to pay the amount of the execution, including penalty, interest and costs. All other proceedings in relation thereto shall be as provided by the Code and Charter of the city and the laws of Georgia. The defendants at execution shall have the rights of defense by affidavit of illegality of the tax or otherwise as provided by the Charter of the city and the laws of Georgia in regard to tax executions. 
(c)  When a nulla bona entry has been entered by proper authority upon an execution, the person, partnership, corporation or other entity against whom the entry is made shall not be allowed or entitled to have or collect any fees or charges whatever for services rendered after the entry of the nulla bona. If, at any time after the entry of nulla bona has been made, the person, partnership, corporation or other entity against whom the execution issues pays the tax in full, together with all interest and costs accrued on the tax, the person may collect any fees and charges due him or her as though he or she had never defaulted in the payment of the tax. 
(d)  A person, partnership, corporation or other entity who fails or refuses to pay any occupation tax charged pursuant to this article shall be subject to a fine, to be imposed by court of competent jurisdiction over enforcement of city's ordinances, not more than $500.00, that may be enforced by the contempt power of the court. 
(e)  A person, partnership, corporation or other entity who fails or refuses to make a timely or truthful tax return or make available truthful and accurate information the city requests or requires for determining applicability or amount of occupation tax or for levying or collecting such occupation tax shall be subject to a fine, to be imposed by court of competent jurisdiction over enforcement of city's ordinances, not more than $500.00, that may be enforced by the contempt power of the court. 
(f)  All persons subject to the occupation tax imposed by this article shall be required to file for and pay such tax or fee. For failure to do so, any officers or agents soliciting for or obtaining business for such person, business or practitioner shall be subject to the same penalty as other persons, businesses or practitioners who fail to make a return for or pay the applicable occupation tax. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-41. - Public hearings. 
(a)  After January 1, 2015, the city shall conduct at least one public hearing before adopting any ordinance or resolution that will increase the occupation tax rate specified in section 18-32. 
(b)  In any year when revenue from occupation taxes is greater than revenue from occupation taxes for the preceding year, the city shall hold one or more public hearing[s] as part of the process of determining how to use the additional revenue. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Sec. 18-42. - Revocation of certificates. 
(a)  All occupation tax certificates granted under this article shall be subject to revocation upon failure of the person, partnership, corporation or other entity to comply with all valid regulations and ordinances of the city regulating the business conducted by or engaged in by such person, partnership, corporation or other entity. 
(b)  Any occupation tax certificates granted under this article may be revoked by the mayor for noncompliance; provided, however, that before there is such revocation, a hearing shall be granted to the person, partnership, corporation or other entity holding such certificate. 
(c)  Any ruling by the mayor adverse to such person, partnership, corporation or other entity shall be subject to review by the city council at the next regular council meeting after the decision by the mayor, upon the filing of a written appeal by the person, partnership, corporation or other entity with the city clerk. The decision of a majority vote of the city council on such appeal shall be final, unless further appeal is allowed by law. 
(d)  No business shall be conducted or engaged in by any person, partnership, corporation or other entity whose certificate has been revoked by the mayor, unless and until the decision of the mayor is reviewed and reversed by majority vote of the city council. 
(Ord. No. 2015-03, § 1, 6-9-15) 
Secs. 18-43—18-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PEDDLERS AND SOLICITORS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Duties of purchasers of gold bullion, gold dust, etc., O.C.G.A. § 12-4-120 et seq.; Georgia Charitable Solicitations Act of 1988, O.C.G.A. § 43-17-1 et seq.; peddlers and itinerant traders, O.C.G.A. § 43-32-1 et seq.; dealers in precious metals and gems, O.C.G.A. § 43-37-1 et seq.; dealers in used watches, O.C.G.A. § 43-49-1 et seq. 

Sec. 18-71. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Peddler means any individual, whether a resident of this city or not, travelling by foot, wagon, automobile, motor truck or any other type of conveyance from place to place, from house to house or from street to street, for the sale of, as well as the selling, offering for sale or taking or attempting to take orders for the sales of goods, wares, merchandise, or personal property of any nature whatsoever, for future delivery, or for services to be furnished or performed in the future, whether or not such individual has, carries or exposes for sale, a sample of the subject of such sale, or whether such individual is collecting advance payments on such sales or not; provided that such definition shall include any person who, for such person's self or for another person, hires, leases, uses or occupies any building, structure, tent, railroad boxcar, boat, hotel room, lodging house, apartment, shop or any other place within the city for the sole purpose of exhibiting samples and taking orders for future delivery. The word "peddler" shall include the terms "canvasser," "solicitor," "transient or itinerant merchant or vendor" or "transient or itinerant photographer." 
(Code 1987, § 13-20) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 18-72. - Exceptions. 
The provisions of this article shall not apply to the following: 
(1)  Sales made to dealers or permanent merchants by commercial travellers selling in the usual course of business; 
(2)  Sheriffs, constables, bona fide assignees, receivers or trustees in bankruptcy or other public officers selling goods, wares and merchandise according to law; 
(3)  Bona fide residents of the state selling fruits, vegetables, dressed meats, fowl or farm products of their own raising. 
(Code 1987, § 13-21) 
Sec. 18-73. - Solicitations not subject to article. 
The following types of solicitations or donations do not come under the provisions of this article: 
(1)  United Fund, United Health and Welfare Fund, and long established agencies accorded similar public approval, but only on single annual drives. 
(2)  Commercial or strictly institutional advertising in recognized publications having established periods of issue of not less than eight per year and similar advertising over radio stations. 
(3)  Donations of merchandise or money as part of regular business promotion. 
(4)  Solicitations of individuals by fellow members of individual clubs for the benefit of that particular organization. 
(5)  Solicitation for membership in any regularly constituted organization. 
(Code 1987, § 13-22) 
Sec. 18-74. - Endorsement of products. 
It will not be the policy of the city to issue any form of written or verbal endorsement of any solicitation, but only to issue a permit upon approval of application to solicit. 
(Code 1987, § 13-23) 
Sec. 18-75. - Behavior of applicants. 
(a)  Refusal to leave. Any peddler who enters upon premises owned, leased, or rented by another and refuses to leave such premises after having been notified by the owner or occupant of such premises, or by such owner's or occupant's agent, to leave the same and not return to such premises, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished accordingly. 
(b)  Entrance to premises restricted. It shall be unlawful for any peddler to enter upon any private premises when such premises are posted with a sign stating "No Peddlers Allowed" or "No Soliciting Allowed" or other words to such effect. Violators shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and punished accordingly. 
(c)  Misrepresentation. It shall be unlawful for any peddler to make false or fraudulent statements concerning the quality of such peddler's goods, wares, merchandise or services for the purpose of inducing another to purchase the same. 
(d)  Hours of operation. It shall be unlawful for any peddler to engage in the business of peddling within the city between the hours of one-half hour before sunset and 9:00 a.m. of the following day, or at any time on Sundays, except by specific appointment with or invitation from the prospective customer. 
(e)  Solicitations at street or highway intersections. It shall be unlawful for any person to solicit funds or distribute literature and/or other materials to motorists or others upon any street or at any intersection in the city or to use any street or intersection in the city for any activity involving the location of any person in such street or intersection in a "roadblock" while the same is open for vehicular traffic. 
(Code 1987, § 13-24) 
Sec. 18-76. - Permit required. 
Every individual desiring to solicit within the city limits must first obtain a permit from the city at the City Hall authorizing such person to solicit. Permits will be issued only to individuals who appear in person at city hall. Under no circumstances will a permit for a group be granted to one individual member of the group unless, in the judgment of the city clerk and/or the mayor, the circumstances allow for such action. 
(Code 1987, § 13-25) 
Sec. 18-77. - Fingerprints. 
At the time of making application for a permit as required by this article, the applicant shall submit to fingerprinting by the chief of police if desired or requested by the city clerk or mayor. 
(Code 1987, § 13-26) 
Sec. 18-78. - Bond. 
(a)  Every applicant, not a resident of this county, or who is a resident of the county and represents a firm whose principal place of business is located outside the state shall, when required by the city clerk or the mayor, file with the city clerk a surety bond running to the city, in the amount of $1,000.00 with surety acceptable to and approved by the mayor, under the condition that the applicant shall comply fully with all applicable provisions of this Code, ordinances of the city, and state law, regulating and concerning the business of peddling and guaranteeing any citizen of the city that all money paid as a down payment will be accounted for and applied according to the representations of the peddler, and further guaranteeing to any citizen of the city doing business with such peddler that the property purchased will be delivered according to the representations of the peddler. Action on such bond may be brought in the name of the city to the use or benefit of the aggrieved person. 
(b)  If the applicant is an agent, employee, canvasser or solicitor of a corporation authorized to do business in this state or registered under the Fictitious Name Act of the state, such corporation or fictitious name business may be required to furnish one bond in the amount of $1,000.00 for all of its agents, employees, canvassers or solicitors. 
(c)  Before any permit shall be issued under this article, there shall, when required under this section, also be filed with the city clerk an instrument in writing, signed by the applicant under oath, nominating and appointing the city clerk as such applicant's true and lawful agent, with full power and authority to acknowledge service of notice or process for and on behalf of such applicant, and service of summons in any action brought upon the applicant's bond shall be deemed made when served on the city clerk. 
(Code 1987, § 13-27) 
Sec. 18-79. - False information. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to give any false or misleading information in connection with such person's application for a permit required by this article. 
(Code 1987, § 13-28) 
Sec. 18-80. - Investigation. 
Upon receipt of an application for a permit required by this article, the original shall be referred to the chief of police, who shall cause such investigation of the applicant's business and moral character to be made as such officer deems necessary for the protection of the public good. The chief of police shall complete such investigation within one week of receiving the application. 
(Code 1987, § 13-29) 
Sec. 18-81. - Denial of permit. 
If, as a result of investigation, the applicant's character or business responsibility is found to be unsatisfactory, the chief of police shall endorse on the application such officer's disapproval and the reasons for same, and shall return the application to the city clerk, who shall notify the applicant that the application is disapproved and that no permit shall be issued. 
(Code 1987, § 13-30) 
Sec. 18-82. - Issuance of permit. 
If, as a result of investigation, the character and business responsibility of the applicant are found to be satisfactory, the chief of police shall endorse such officer's approval on the application and return the application to the city clerk. The city clerk shall prepare the permit for carrying on of the business applied for and deliver same to the applicant. At this time, the applicant shall be advised of the restrictions prescribed by this article and advise the applicant of the penalties involved in case of noncompliance. 
(Code 1987, § 13-31) 
Sec. 18-83. - Contents of permit. 
Each permit issued under this article shall show the name and address of the permittee, the purpose for which the permit is issued, the firm represented, the items being sold and to whose benefit the receipts will accrue, date of issuance, period of time for which permit is valid, the permit number and identification of any vehicle to be used in such solicitation. 
(Code 1987, § 13-32) 
Sec. 18-84. - Revocation of permit. 
Any permit issued under the provisions of this article may be revoked by the mayor or city clerk for the violation by the permittee of any applicable provision of this article, the city code, state law or other city ordinance, rule or regulation. 
(Code 1987, § 13-33) 
Sec. 18-85. - Withdrawal of permit. 
In case where it is found that the permittee is in violation of this article, contact shall be made with the permittee by a member of the police department, who shall advise permittee of the reported violation and shall secure the permit and return same to the city clerk. 
(Code 1987, § 13-34) 
Sec. 18-86. - Record. 
The city clerk shall maintain a permanent record of all permits issued under this article. 
(Code 1987, § 13-35) 
Sec. 18-87. - Display. 
Each peddler having a permit issued under the provisions of this article and doing business within the city shall display the permit upon request of any person, and failure to do so shall render the permit null and void. 
(Code 1987, § 13-36) 
Sec. 18-88. - Duration. 
Each permit issued under the provisions of this article shall be valid only for a period of time stated thereon, but in no event shall any such permit be issued for a period of time in excess of 12 months. 
(Code 1987, § 13-37) 
Secs. 18-89—18-115. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - INSURERS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Persons deemed professional bondsmen, O.C.G.A. § 17-6-50; local tax on life insurance companies, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.1; local tax on other than life insurance companies, O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2; general assembly authorized to provide for taxation of insurance companies based on gross direct premiums received from insurance policies within the unincorporated areas of counties, Ga. Const. art. IX, § IV, ¶ I(c). 

Sec. 18-116. - Insurer license fees—Company. 
There is hereby levied an annual license fee upon each insurer doing business within the city in the amount of $40.00. For each separate business location in excess of one not covered by section 18-117, which is operating on behalf of such insurers within the city, there is hereby levied a license fee in the amount of $40.00. For the purposes of this article, the term "insurer" means a company which is authorized to transact business in the classes of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5. 
(Code 1987, § 13-40; Ord. of 1-8-91, § 1) 
Sec. 18-117. - Same—Insuring certain risks at additional business locations. 
For each separate business location, not otherwise subject to a license fee under this article, operated and maintained by a business organization which is engaged in the business of lending money or transacting sales involving term financing and in connection with such loans or sales, offers, solicits or takes application for insurance through a licensed agent of an insurer for insurance said insurer shall pay an additional license fee of $40.00 per location for each year. 
(Code 1987, § 13-41; Ord. of 1-8-91, § 2) 
Sec. 18-118. - Same—Agency; independent insurance agencies, brokers, etc. not otherwise licensed. 
There is hereby levied an annual license fee upon independent agencies and brokers for each separate business location from which an insurance business is conducted and which is not subject to the company license fee imposed by section 18-116, in the amount of $40.00 for each such location within the city. 
(Code 1987, § 13-42; Ord. of 1-8-91, § 3) 
Sec. 18-119. - Gross premiums tax—Life insurers. 
There is hereby levied an annual tax based solely upon gross direct premiums upon each insurer writing life, accident and sickness insurance within the city in an amount equal to one percent of the gross direct premiums received during the preceding calendar year in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.1. Gross direct premiums as used in this section shall mean gross direct premiums as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-4. The premium tax levied by this section is in addition to the license fees imposed by section 18-116. 
(Code 1987, § 13-43; Ord. of 1-8-91, § 4) 
Sec. 18-120. - Same—All other insurers. 
There is hereby levied an annual tax upon each insurer, other than an insurer transacting business in the class of insurance designated in O.C.G.A. § 33-3-5(1), doing business within the city in an amount equal to 2½ percent of the gross direct premiums received during the preceding calendar year, in accordance with O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2. Gross direct premiums as used in this section shall mean gross direct premiums as used in O.C.G.A. § 33-8-8.2(a). 
(Code 1987, § 13-44; Ord. of 1-8-91, § 5) 
Sec. 18-121. - Due date for license fees. 
License fees imposed in sections 18-116, 18-117 and 18-118 shall be due and payable on March 1 of each year. 
(Code 1987, § 13-45; Ord. of 1-8-91, § 6) 
Sec. 18-122. - Reports—Filing; contents. 
Payments required by this article shall be made to the city clerk and shall be accompanied by a report showing the names and addresses of the agents representing the insurance company in the city, the classes of insurance written, the premiums received for each class, and such other reasonable information as may be required. The required report shall be made on forms prescribed by the city clerk and made out over affidavit of an officer of the company. Payments shall be deemed delinquent if not received within 45 days from the due date. 
(Code 1987, § 13-46) 
Sec. 18-123. - Same—False information; confidentiality. 
(a)  False information. It is hereby declared to be a violation of this article for any person to knowingly give false or incomplete information on any report herein required to be filed. 
(b)  Confidentiality of information. All reports required to be filed shall be confidential and the information contained therein shall be used solely by the officers of the city responsible for the administration of this article. 
(Code 1987, § 13-47) 
Sec. 18-124. - Enforcement. 
The taxes levied by this article may be enforced by execution in the same manner as other taxes of this city. 
(Code 1987, § 13-48) 
Secs. 18-125—18-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - DEALERS IN PRECIOUS METALS AND GEMS, PAWNSHOPS AND SECONDHAND DEALERS[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, adopted Aug. 8, 2017, amended art. V in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former art. V, §§ 18-151—18-157 was entitled "Pawnbrokers and Secondhand Dealers," and derived from Ord. No. 2014-04, § 1, adopted Nov. 11, 2014. 
State Law reference— Duties of purchasers of gold bullion, gold dust, etc., O.C.G.A. § 12-4-120 et seq.; junk dealers, O.C.G.A. § 43-22-1 et seq.; dealers in precious metals and gems, O.C.G.A. § 43-37-1 et seq.; dealers in used watches, O.C.G.A. § 43-49-1 et seq.; liens—pawnbrokers, factors, bailees, etc., O.C.G.A. § 44-14-400 et seq.; liens—jewelers, O.C.G.A. § 44-14-430 et seq. 

Sec. 18-151. - Definitions. 
For the purposes of this article (article V - Dealers in Precious Metals and Gems, Pawnshops and Secondhand Dealers), the following words and terms shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them: 
Dealer in precious metals and gems means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, who engages in the business of purchasing precious metals or gems or articles containing any precious metal or gem, including coins, from a member of the general public for resale to brokers, dealers or melters. 
Electronic reporting system means a computer based system, as specified by the chief of police, which is designed to record and transmit data and information electronically. 
Gems means any precious or semi-precious stone which is cut and polished. 
Goods means every species of tangible personal property. 
Pawnbroker means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, engaged in whole or in part in the business of lending money on the security of pledged goods, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property on the condition that it may be redeemed or repurchased by the seller for a fixed price within a fixed period of time, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property from persons or sources other than manufacturers or licensed dealers as a part of or in conjunction with the business activities described in this section. 
Pawnshop means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, engaged in whole or in part in the business of lending money on the security of pledged goods, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property on the condition that it may be redeemed or repurchased by the seller for a fixed price within a fixed period of time, or in the business of purchasing tangible personal property from persons or sources other than manufacturers or licensed dealers as a part of or in conjunction with the business activities described in this section. 
Person means an individual, partnership, corporation, joint venture, trust, association, or other legal entity however organized. 
Precious metals means gold, silver or platinum or any metal containing gold, silver or platinum. 
Secondhand dealer means any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, whose business includes purchasing, storing, selling, exchanging, or receiving secondhand personal property of any kind or description. However, any person, whether as owner, agent or employee, whose business is the purchase and resale of clothing, furniture, or the resale of goods that are donated to a business exempt from federal taxation as a charitable organization shall not be deemed a secondhand dealer under this article. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-152. - Penalty for violation of article. 
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this article shall be punished upon conviction in the state court as provided in section 1-6. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-153. - License required. 
It shall be unlawful for a buyer of precious metals and gems to engage in such business within the county without first obtaining a license in compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-154. - Application for license. 
Applicants for a license pursuant to this article shall file with the city clerk a written application under oath, signed by the applicant if an individual, or by all partners if a partnership, or by the president of the corporation, and showing the following: 
(1)  The name of the person having the management or supervision of the applicant's business during the time that it is proposed that it will be carried on within the city; the local address of such person while engaged in such business; the permanent address of such person; the capacity in which such person will act, that is, whether as proprietor, agent or otherwise; the name and address of the person on whose account the business will be conducted, if any; and, if a corporation, the name of the state in which the corporation is incorporated; 
(2)  The place within the city where it is proposed to conduct the applicant's business, and the length of time during which it is proposed that such business will be conducted; 
(3)  Credentials from the person for which the applicant proposes to do business, authorizing the applicant to act as representative; and 
(4)  Such other reasonable information as to the identity and character of the person having the management or supervision of the business and the manner of doing business as the city council may deem proper in order to fulfill the purpose of this article in the protection of the public interest. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-155. - Bond. 
(a)  Before any license shall be issued pursuant to this article, the applicant shall file with the city clerk a bond binding the applicant to the city in the full sum of $10,000.00, executed by the applicant as principal and by a surety approved by the county commission, conditioned on the applicant's full compliance with the ordinances of the city and the statutes of the state governing the conduct of such business and will pay all judgments rendered against the applicant for any violation of such ordinances or statutes. Action on the bond may be brought in the name of the city in its own behalf. 
(b)  Before any license shall be issued pursuant to this article, the applicant shall file with the city clerk an instrument appointing the clerk of the city as his true and lawful agent for service of process upon the applicant for the performance of the conditions of the bond or for any breach thereof. Immediately upon service of process upon the clerk of the city as provided in this article, the clerk shall send to the licensee, at his last known address, by registered mail, a copy of such process. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-156. - Posting of license. 
The license issued pursuant to this article shall be posted conspicuously and prominently in the place of business named therein. If the applicant desires to do business in more than one place within the county, separate licenses shall be purchased and issued for each place of business, and shall be posted conspicuously and prominently in each place of business. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-157. - License fee. 
Licensees under this article shall pay a license fee of $50.00 for each calendar year or portion of a year in which the licensee engages in business within the county. For each business location in addition to one, the licensee shall pay an additional license fee of $50.00 for each calendar year or portion of a year in which the licensee conducts business at such additional location. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-158. - Revocation of license. 
(a)  The license issued pursuant to this article may be revoked by the chairman and county commission, after notice and hearing, for any of the following causes: 
(1)  Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the application for license; 
(2)  Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in connection with any purchase transaction; 
(3)  Failure to maintain the daily record as required in this article; 
(4)  Any other violation of this article; or 
(5)  Conducting the business licensed under this article in any unlawful manner or in such a manner as to constitute a breach of the peace or to constitute a menace to the health, safety or general welfare of the public. 
(b)  Notice of hearing for revocation of a license shall be given in writing, setting forth specifically the grounds of the complaint and the time and place of the hearing. The notice shall be served on the licensee by handing the notice personally to the person in charge of the licensee's business, or by mailing the notice, postage prepaid, to the licensee, at his last known address, at least five days prior to the date set for the hearing. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-159. - Records and information to be recorded. 
Every person or business engaged as a pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, or dealer in precious metals and gems within the county shall secure from every person from whom he or she receives any goods, except used books, whether by purchase or through pledge, trade, pawn or exchange, the following: 
(1)  Government-issued photo identification card, such as a driver's license, military identification card, state identification card or passport; 
(2)  The name, address, telephone number, race, sex, height, weight, date of birth, and a Social Security or driver's license number; 
(3)  A digital photograph clearly showing a frontal view of the subject's face. Each digital image shall be labeled with the date and time of the transaction and stored in such a manner that they are safe from corruption. If the same subject makes additional transactions within 30 days of the original transaction; provides the same government issued photo identification card as mentioned above; and the subject's appearance has not materially changed, a new digital photograph shall not be required until a transaction is made after 30 days from the original transaction; 
(4)  A complete and accurate description of the goods acquired, and a digital photograph or image of the goods acquired including the following information, if available: 
a.  Brand name; 
b.  Model number; 
c.  Manufacturer's serial number; 
d.  Size; 
e.  Color, as apparent to the untrained eye; 
f.  Precious metal type, weight, and content if known; 
g.  Gemstone description, including the number of stones; 
h.  In the case of firearms, the type of action, caliber or gauge, number of barrels, barrel length, and finish; 
i.  Any other unique identifying marks, numbers, or letters; 
j.  The date and time of the transaction. 
(5)  The pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, and dealer in precious metals and gems shall maintain the above information and digital photographs or images for a period of three years and make the same available to law enforcement personnel upon request. 
(6)  The pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, and dealer in precious metals and gems shall require the seller to sign a statement verifying that the seller is the rightful owner of the goods or is entitled to sell, consign, or trade the goods. 
(7)  This section shall not apply to the receipt of used books or pawn transactions commonly known as "title pawn" transactions where the pawnbroker takes possession of a motor vehicle certificate of title, takes a security interest in the motor vehicle certificate of title, and retains physical possession of the vehicle certificate of title for the entire length of the pawn transaction. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-160. - Report to chief of police; required format. 
(a)  Every pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, and dealer in precious metals and gems located within the county shall make a computer-generated daily report, in such format as prescribed by the Chief of Police for the City of Blackshear, Georgia, of all transactions that occurred during the 24-hour period ending at 9:00 p.m. on the date of the report. A report shall be made each day prior to 11:59 p.m. for each day the operator or dealer transacts business. If an operator or dealer is closed, or does not otherwise engage in any transactions on a particular day, a report indicating "no transactions" shall be filed for that day. Daily reports shall be filed electronically by posting to a law enforcement web site designated by the chief of police. When technological problems prevent posting the daily report electronically, a printed, typed or legibly handwritten report shall be delivered to the City of Blackshear Police Department. 
(b)  This section shall not apply to the receipt of used books or pawn transactions commonly known as "title pawn" transactions where the pawnbroker takes possession of a motor vehicle certificate of title; takes a security interest in the motor vehicle certificate of title, and retains physical possession of the vehicle certificate of title for the entire length of the pawn transaction. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-161. - Hold period; police holds. 
(a)  Any pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, dealer in precious metals and gems, or person operating under a license granted pursuant to this article who takes goods on pawn or who buys goods, taking full title thereto, shall hold the goods so taken in pawn for at least 30 days before disposing of the goods by sale, transfer, shipment or otherwise. 
(b)  The Blackshear Police Department or any other law enforcement agency, has the authority to place property that is the subject of law enforcement investigation on "police hold". In that event, Blackshear Police Department, or other law enforcement agency, shall notify the pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, or dealer in precious metals and gems of the need for a "police hold" and identify all property subject to the "police hold". Upon notification, it shall be the responsibility of the pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, or dealer in precious metals and gems to maintain the subject property until such time as the property is released from "police hold" status or the property is confiscated as evidence. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Sec. 18-162. - Unlawful acts. 
It shall be unlawful for pawnbroker, pawnshop, secondhand dealer, dealer in precious metals and gems or person operating under a license granted pursuant to this article to commit any of the following acts: 
(1)  Fail to make an entry of any material matter in the daily record of said business; 
(2)  Make any false entry in the daily record of said business; 
(3)  Falsify, obliterate or destroy the daily record of said business or remove the daily record from the place of business; 
(4)  Refuse to allow any duly authorized law enforcement officer to inspect the daily record of said business or any goods in the possession of said business during the ordinary hours of business or at any reasonable time; or 
(5)  Fail to comply with this article in any other material way. 
(Ord. No. 2017-04, § 1, 8-8-17) 
Secs. 18-163—18-190. - Reserved. 
Chapter 22 - CEMETERIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2013-09, §§ 1—4, adopted July 9, 2013, amended ch. 22 in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former ch. 22, §§ 22-1—22-7, pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Code 1987, §§ 6-1—6-7. 
Cross reference— Streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66. 
State Law reference— Criminal trespass and damage to property, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-20 et seq.; abandoned cemeteries and burial grounds, O.C.G.A. § 36-72-1 et seq.; Georgia Cemetery Act of 1983, O.C.G.A. § 44-3-130 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 22-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Casket means an ornamented and lined rectangular box used to place human remains in for burial. 
Cemetery means the Blackshear Cemetery, as shown and depicted on all recorded and unrecorded plats. 
Cemetery superintendent means an employee of the city designated by the city manager to supervise cemetery operations. 
Coping means a raised border surrounding grave spaces or lots. 
Cremains or cremated remains means residual ash fragments of human bones remaining after the process of cremation. 
Cremation means the process of reducing human remains to ash through incineration. 
Deceased human being or human remains or remains means the body or bodies of deceased persons, including bodies in any stage of decomposition and cremated remains. 
Deed means the document issued only by the city that conveys ownership interest in a lot in the cemetery. 
Deferred payment plan means a method of paying for a lot or lots by first depositing a portion of the total cost of the lot or lots with the city with the stipulation that the balance will be paid within 12 months. 
Disinterment means removal of human remains from a grave. 
Grave or grave space means an area of ground sufficient for the burial of human remains. See also lot. 
Indigent means a destitute person. 
Interment means burial of human remains in a grave. 
Lot means one or more adjoining grave spaces. 
Lot owner means one or more individuals whose names are shown on the deed. Any individual names on the deed may give written instructions to the city. 
Marker means a small individual memorial placed at either the head or foot of a grave. 
Memorial means a marker, monument or vase placed on a lot and shall include any monument, memorial, marker, or vase in whole or in part at ground level or above ground, or other structure on the cemetery lot. 
Monument means a large slab placed flat on a lot. 
Urn means a receptacle of cast bronze, marble, or other acceptable permanent material containing cremated remains, which is placed in the ground. 
Vault means a reinforced concrete container used in the above or below ground burial of human remains in which the casket is placed. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-2. - Reserved. 
Sec. 22-3. - No liability for damages. 
The city will not be held responsible for any vandalism or damages to any memorial, monument, urn or marker. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-4. - Management; appointment of cemetery superintendent. 
The control and management of the cemetery shall be under the direct supervision of the mayor, who shall administer this chapter. He shall assign a city employee as cemetery superintendent to take charge of burials and ensure the operational integrity of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-5. - Duties of cemetery superintendent. 
The cemetery superintendent shall issue burial permits and refuse burial until the permit and related or required documents comply with state law and the provisions of the City Code. The cemetery superintendent shall inspect the closed grave to insure that the remaining fill has been removed from the gravesite. The cemetery superintendent shall do all other work required in the operation of the cemetery. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-6. - Executing instructions. 
(a)  In all cases where a lot is owned by more than one person, the city may act upon the authority of any one of the owners. If all lot owners desire that no instructions be followed unless signed by all lot owners shown on the deed, all lot owners must submit a signed and notarized statement with that request. 
(b)  All matters relating to the opening of graves, the interment of remains, disinterments, and reinterments shall be in writing from the lot owner. The city shall not execute instructions given by any other means. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-7. - City's right to correct errors. 
(a)  The city shall have the right to correct any errors that may be made by it in good faith by taking such actions as it deems necessary and appropriate in the circumstances. If the error shall involve the interment of remains, the city shall have the right, at its expense, to remove and reinter the remains to another lot of equal value and similar location. 
(b)  The city shall have the right to correct any error it may make in placement of any memorial, marker, vase, or vault. The city shall not be liable for any error so made. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-8. - Fees, gratuities and commissions. 
No city employee shall receive any fee, gratuity or commission either directly or indirectly, except from the city or work performed in the cemetery. No city employee shall influence the city in regard to any allied service or commodity under penalty of immediate dismissal. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 1, 7-9-13) 
Secs. 22-9—22-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - LOTS 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 22-36. - Subdivision of cemetery. 
The Blackshear City Council shall have sole authority to subdivide the cemetery into divisions, blocks, sections, lots, grave spaces, and streets, and to determine the dimensions and locations of each. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-37. - City's right to replat, regrade and use property. 
(a)  The city reserves the right to replat any parts of the property within the cemetery not sold for burial purposes, including the right to open, close, or change the location or grade of streets or walkways. The city shall have a perpetual right of ingress and egress over lots for the purpose of passage to and from other lots when no other means of passage is available. 
(b)  The city reserves the right to close and sell the grounds lying between lots, known as walkways, provided that by said closing adequate access to adjoining lots is provided. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-38. - Sale, place of payment; cemetery fund. 
(a)  Sale of lots. The sale of lots shall be by deed. A comprehensive record of the cemetery deeds, plats, and other records related thereto, shall be kept by the city clerk. The record shall show all lots which are sold or are for sale and a record made of the date, name of the purchaser, division or block, section, lot and grave number. A deed shall be issued upon the receipt of full payment, naming any special restrictions, which are not embodied in this chapter, and signed by the proper city officials. 
(b)  Place of payment; cemetery fund. All payments for the sale of lots and all service charges shall be payable to the city at the Blackshear City Hall. All executed deeds shall be delivered to the owner through the city clerk. All receipts from the sale of cemetery lots, burial fees, and beautification services shall be placed in the cemetery fund. Money placed in this fund shall only be used for cemetery purposes. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-39. - Charges; bulk purchases. 
(a)  The price for the purchase of grave space shall be according to the following schedule: 
(1)  All grave spaces located in Blackshear Cemetery shall be sold for a sum to be set by resolution of the Blackshear City Council. 
(2)  The city will provide a grave space for an indigent who is a city resident. Proof of residency and indigency shall be provided by signed affidavits, provided by the funeral home. The grave space will be determined by cemetery superintendent. 
(b)  Any cemetery lot purchase in excess of eight lots requires written justification by the applicant and approval by the mayor. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-40. - Deferred payment plan. 
(a)  A prospective purchaser of grave lots may purchase up to four lots on a deferred payment plan. A written agreement will be required. Upon signing the agreement, a payment of one-fourth of the total cost of all the lots to be purchased shall be required. The balance will be due within 12 months. No interest shall be required during the initial, 12-month term of the agreement. If the balance is not paid in full within 12 months, one extension of six months may be allowed, and interest may be charged. In the case of an agreement for multiple lots, payments made will be credited to an individual lot, and when sufficient payments have been received to cover the cost of one lot, a deed may be issued for that lot. 
(b)  If the purchaser fails to make full payment within the time period allocated, the city reserves the right to cancel the agreement. At the time of cancellation of the agreement, the city may list the grave lots for sale, and the purchaser shall have no right to any of the lots covered under the agreement. A deed will be issued for any lots which have been paid for in full during the term of the agreement. If the agreement has been cancelled for nonpayment, and the city has not received enough money to pay for a lot in full, the city may impose a cancellation fee to be established by the Blackshear City Council by resolution, and will then return any balance to the purchaser. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-41. - Reserved. 
Sec. 22-42. - Correct mailing address of lot owners. 
Each lot owner shall have the duty to keep the city informed as to his or her correct mailing address. Any notice mailed to a lot owner at the last address on file with the city shall be equivalent to actual delivery of the notice. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-43. - Transfer of ownership. 
(a)  No lot owner shall allow interment in his or her lot for a remuneration, nor shall any transfer of interest in the lot be valid except by written consent of the city. Such transfer or assignment shall be recorded in the records of the cemetery. No transfer for consideration shall be authorized. Any attempted transfer of a lot or interest in a lot to one not authorized to own the lot shall be invalid and of no force and effect. The city shall not be obligated to honor the transfer. 
(b)  The city may refuse to consent to a transfer or to an assignment as long as there is any indebtedness due the city from the lot owner for interment rights in the lot involved. 
(c)  In every case where a lot owner wishes to dispose of vacant lots, the city shall have the option to repurchase the lot at a price agreed upon between the lot owner and the official representative of the city. The price shall not exceed 75 percent of the original purchase price, including perpetual care. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-44. - Decorations. 
(a)  No permanent flower receptacles may be placed on any lot unless, of an approved size, material and design, set wholly beneath the level of the grass. Only one vase will be permitted for each marker or grave space. 
(b)  Potted plants, wreaths, floral arrangements, metal emblems, markers, or flags may be permitted upon lots on holidays. If not removed within five days, said decorations may, at the option of the city, be removed. Potted plants, wreaths and floral arrangements will be removed from the lot or grave at the time of mowing or trimming the grass. 
(c)  The city shall have the right to remove all floral arrangements, wreaths and the like as soon after a funeral as in the judgment of the city they become wilted or unsightly. 
(d)  The city shall not be responsible for any items of decoration that become lost, misplaced or damaged. 
(e)  The city shall not be responsible for plantings damaged by the elements, thieves, vandals, or by other causes beyond its control. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Secs. 22-45—22-55. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PERPETUAL CARE 

Sec. 22-56. - Perpetual care trust fund. 
There is established a perpetual care trust fund known as the Blackshear Cemetery Trust Fund. All money received from the owners of lots in the ancient section for perpetual care, together with 65 percent of the money received from the sale of the lots, shall be paid to the city and deposited in the fund. The city shall invest such funds in accordance with city investment policy. The income from the trust fund shall be used exclusively for the care and maintenance of the lots and cemetery grounds. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-57. - Perpetual care services; fees. 
(a)  Perpetual care service shall consist of cutting, trimming, top dressing, and annual fertilizing of all grass area. Any additional care desired will be the responsibility of the owner. All owners of grave spaces for which perpetual care has not been previously included shall purchase perpetual care prior to the opening and closing of a grave and shall pay the city a sum to be set by resolution of the Blackshear City Council. 
(b)  Upon the payment of the perpetual care fee, the cemetery superintendent or designee is authorized to deliver to the purchaser a certificate evidencing the purchase, signed by him or her on behalf of the city. Full perpetual care payment for a grave space or lot must be paid prior to interment. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 2, 7-9-13) 
Secs. 22-58—22-80. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - INTERMENT 

Sec. 22-81. - Burial permit required; cost. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any undertaker or other person legally entitled to bury the body of a deceased human being without first securing from the cemetery superintendent a burial permit signed by the cemetery superintendent or his or her designee. A burial permit shall be issued only when all laws, ordinances, rules and regulations relative to burials have been complied with and all fees and costs previously billed by the city have been paid. The cemetery superintendent may request a properly executed death certificate or a burial transit permit of the decedent. The burial permit shall show the name, address, sex, age, place of burial, and any other details and information as the cemetery superintendent may require. 
(b)  The charge for a burial permit shall be a sum set by resolution of the Blackshear City Council. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 3, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-82. - Prerequisites to burial; charges; minimum depth of graves. 
(a)  The opening and closing of all graves shall be conducted under the supervision of the city. No burial shall be performed in the cemetery without the completion of state prescribed burial forms by a sub-registrar. A burial permit shall be obtained from the cemetery superintendent before the interment of any human remains. 
(b)  To verify that a monument is installed on the proper grave and to mark and inspect the installation of a monument, marker, memorial or coping, there shall be a fee set by resolution of the Blackshear City Council. 
(c)  The minimum depth of all graves shall be 4½ feet; the minimum depth for vaults shall be 3½ feet. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 3, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-83. - Regulations for interments and disinterments. 
(a)  All interments and disinterments shall be made subject to state law, city ordinances, and operating rules and regulations of the cemetery. 
(b)  No interment will be made without written authority from the owner or one of the owners of the lot in question. If there is more than one owner, no disinterment will be made without the written consent of all owners or upon presentation of a court order. Disinterments shall be made at the city's convenience. 
(c)  All disinterments shall be done by or under the supervision of the cemetery superintendent. The cemetery will exercise the utmost care in making a removal, but it assumes no liability for damage to any casket or urn incurred in the process of making a removal. 
(d)  When instructions regarding the location of an interment space in a lot cannot be obtained, are indefinite, or when for any reason the interment space cannot be opened where specified, the city may, in its discretion, open a space in another location in the lot as it deems best and proper, so as not to delay the funeral. 
(e)  Not more than one body shall be interred in any one grave space, except in cases where a parent and infant child, or two infant children, are buried at the same time. In such cases, only one memorial shall be permitted; however, the memorial may bear both names. Cremated remains may be interred at the foot of a grave space. The name of the person may be combined with an adjoining single marker, or incorporated into a companion marker for both graves. Two cremated remains instead of one body may be interred into a grave space. In that case, a single marker designating the two cremated remains may be installed in the grave space. 
(f)  No interment of any body or the cremated remains of any body, other than that of a human being, shall be permitted. 
(g)  Removal, by the heirs, of a body so that the lot may be sold for profit to themselves, or removal contrary to the expressed or implied wish of the original lot owners shall not be permitted. 
(h)  Besides being subject to the rules and regulations set out in this article, all interments, disinterments, and removals are subject to the orders and laws of the properly constituted authorities of the city, Pierce County and the State of Georgia. 
(i)  At the expense of the family a body or cremated remains may be removed from its original lot to a larger or more desirable lot in the cemetery where there has been an exchange or purchase for that purpose. 
(j)  Once a casket containing a body is within the confines of the cemetery, no funeral director, embalmer, assistant, employee, or agent shall be permitted to open a casket or to touch the body without the consent of the legal representative of the deceased, a relative in charge of the funeral, or a court order. 
(k)  All interments and disinterments must be made at the time, in the manner, and upon the charges as fixed from time to time by the city. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 3, 7-9-13) 
Secs. 22-84—22-105. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - REGULATIONS 

Sec. 22-106. - Visitors; proper conduct. 
(a)  Visiting hours are restricted to daylight hours and shall be as specified by the city. Any unauthorized person(s) found in the cemetery after dark will be considered a trespasser. 
(b)  In order that the proper atmosphere may be maintained at the cemetery, children under 15 years of age, unless attended by an adult responsible for their conduct, and persons having firearms in their possession, except military personnel, law enforcement personnel and honor guards in attendance upon a funeral, are prohibited from entering the cemetery. 
(c)  In order to safeguard the quiet and peaceful atmosphere of the cemetery visitors are prohibited from using loud, boisterous or obscene language from sitting or climbing on markers, monuments, or fixtures of any kind; from peddling, begging, soliciting, or collecting; and from displaying or distributing cards, handbills and circulars of any nature, unless approved by the cemetery superintendent. 
(d)  Visitors are prohibited from bringing into the cemetery dogs, other than guide dogs for the handicapped, and alcoholic beverages. Visitors are prohibited from removing, scratching, marring, defacing, injuring, or disturbing any monument, memorial bench, vase, building, fence, or anything within the limits of the cemetery; and from putting paper, rubbish, dead or wilted flowers, shrubs, plants, or any other unsightly or improper thing in any place except in the containers provided for such materials. Persons within the cemetery shall use only the walks and roads. No person shall gather flowers, damage trees, shrubbery or plants. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 4, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-107. - Planting of trees, shrubs and other improvements. 
(a)  The city undertakes to maintain, as nearly as may be practical, the plantings of trees and shrubs which serve as a backdrop on the cemetery grounds and to preserve the landscape features, but it does not undertake to maintain plants upon individual lots. 
(b)  Permanent planting of grass, shrubs, flowers, and the like shall be made by the city. Further planting may be permitted only at the discretion of the city and with a permit issued by the cemetery superintendent. The ownership of lots or grave spaces does not convey any right to do planting without the express approval of the city. 
(c)  No elevated mounds shall be built over graves and no lot shall be filled above the grade established by the cemetery superintendent. 
(d)  If any tree, shrub or plant standing upon any lot, by means of its roots, branches or otherwise, be or become detrimental to adjacent lots, walks or streets, or if for any reason its removal is deemed necessary, the cemetery superintendent shall have the right and duty to remove the tree, plant or shrub or any part thereof, or otherwise correct the existing condition. 
(e)  No planting of flowers, shrubs, or herbage of any kind is permitted on single graves. All improvements and planting on lots shall be subject to prior approval of the cemetery superintendent. Any improvement or planting made on a lot by or for a lot owner without prior approval may be removed by the cemetery superintendent at the expense of the lot owner. 
(f)  No trees, shrubs, plants, or herbage of any kind shall be removed from any lot without the prior consent of the cemetery superintendent. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 4, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-108. - Vehicle operation. 
(a)  All motor vehicles must be operated within the limits of the cemetery in a quiet, safe and orderly manner. Vehicles shall be driven at not more than 15 miles per hour, shall be driven on streets provided, and shall be operated in accordance with the laws of the city and the state. All vehicles shall be parked on the streets in a manner that will permit other vehicles to pass without leaving the street. 
(b)  Except in the performance of duties within the cemetery grounds or in unusual circumstances, vehicles other than passenger cars and funeral cars, and in particular, trucks, bicycles, motorcycles, and motorbikes, are prohibited from entering the cemetery gates. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 4, 7-9-13) 
Sec. 22-109. - Memorial and vault installations. 
All memorial work shall be done between the hours of 8:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. on weekdays. Persons in charge of memorial work shall notify the cemetery superintendent prior to entering the cemetery to perform the work, and must procure the required permit in accordance with subsection 22-82(b) for each setting. All memorial work must comply with the standards as provided by the cemetery superintendent. 
(Ord. No. 2013-09, § 4, 7-9-13) 
Secs. 22-110—22-135. - Reserved. 
Chapter 26 - CIVIL EMERGENCIES[1] 
Footnotes:

Editor's note— The Pierce County Emergency Operations Plan was approved by city and county officials in 1995. It will be activated by the county emergency management director when directed by the chairman of the board of commissioners of the county or when an emergency is declared by the governor. An official copy of such plan is on file in the office of the county clerk. 
Cross reference— Fire prevention and protection, ch. 38; floods, ch. 42.

Chapter 30 - COURTS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference— Municipal court, § 5.10 et seq. 
Cross reference— Offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 50; traffic and vehicles, ch. 70. 
State Law reference— Powers of presiding officer in court of a municipal corporation to bind over or commit criminal offenders to jail, O.C.G.A. § 17-7-22; municipal courts, O.C.G.A. § 36-32-1 et seq.; agreements between private entities and municipal court judges for probation services, O.C.G.A. § 42-8-102; establishment of municipal courts authorized and jurisdiction thereof, Ga. Const. art. VI, § I, ¶ I. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 30-1—30-29. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MUNICIPAL COURT 

Sec. 30-30. - Municipal court proceedings date and time. 
(a)  The Municipal Court of the City of Blackshear shall convene on the third Friday of every month beginning at 9:00 a.m. This change in court date and time shall take effect beginning on the third Friday of July, 2014, and until such time, the regular court date of the second Tuesday of every month shall remain in effect. 
(b)  The chief judge of municipal court, in consultation with the chief of police, shall have the authority to convene the municipal court for special sessions as necessary to accommodate case scheduling and case load requirements. 
(Ord. No. 2014-01, §§ 1, 2, 4-8-14) 
Sec. 30-31. - Bailiff. 
(a)  The bailiff of the municipal court shall be appointed by the mayor, by and with the advice and consent of city council. 
(b)  The duties of the bailiff shall consist generally of seeing that the courtroom is in proper condition for sessions of court, of assisting in keeping order while court is in session, and of doing such other acts of assistance as may be required of such bailiff by the judge of the court and the city clerk. 
(Code 1987, § 8-4) 
Sec. 30-32. - Record of cases. 
A record of all cases heard in the municipal court for violation of this Code or other municipal ordinances shall be kept in a suitable bound volume by the city clerk. Such records shall contain the name of the defendant, the nature of the offense charged, the final disposition of the case, and the date of final disposition. 
(Code 1987, § 8-5) 
Sec. 30-33. - Additional methods for giving, forfeiture and collection of appearance bonds. 
(a)  When any person is charged with an offense against the laws or ordinances of the City of Blackshear or other cases subject to trial in the city municipal court, or when any person is arrested for any such offense, such person shall: 
(1)  Give bond for his or her appearance at any session of the city municipal court in the same manner as bonds are given for appearance in the state superior courts; or 
(2)  Give bond in any manner now provided by the Charter, Code, ordinances, resolutions of the city, and laws of the state applicable to the city municipal court. 
(b)  If any person so charged shall fail to appear at the time appointed in said bond, then and in such event said bond or recognizance shall be forfeited and the amount of same collected from the principal and his sureties thereon as set forth herein. 
(c)  A bond forfeiture proceeding shall be commenced immediately upon the failure of appearance of a principal of any bond or recognizance given for the appearance of that person. 
(d)  Execution (forfeiture) hearing: 
(1)  The judge of the municipal court shall, upon the failure of the principal to appear, set an execution hearing for a date within 30 days after said failure to appear or as soon thereafter as the case may be heard. Notice of the hearing shall be mailed by first class mail by the clerk of the court to the principal and to each surety at the addresses given on the bond. 
(2)  If at the hearing it is determined that the bond should be forfeited, the judge shall so order and an execution on the order shall immediately be issued. 
(e)  Nonappearance; when no judgment shall be rendered decreeing forfeiture: 
(1)  No judgment shall be rendered decreeing the forfeiture of any appearance bond if it is shown to the satisfaction of the court by the sworn statement of a reputable physician that the principal in the bond was prevented from attending by some physical disability.
