(1)  In the event that any city employee responsible for or involved in restoring an existing covered account or accepting payment for a covered account becomes aware of red flags indicating possible identity theft with respect to existing covered accounts, such employee shall use his or her discretion to determine whether such red flag or combination of red flags suggests a threat of identity theft. If, in his or her discretion, such employee determines that identity theft or attempted identity theft is likely or probable, such employee shall immediately report such red flags to the city administrator. If, in his or her discretion, such employee deems that identity theft is unlikely or that reliable information is available to reconcile red flags, the employee shall convey this information to the city administrator, who may in his or her discretion determine that no further action is necessary. If the city administrator in his or her discretion determines that further action is necessary, a city employee shall perform one or more of the following responses, as determined to be appropriate by the city administrator: 
a.  Contact the customer; 
b.  Make the following changes to the account if, after contacting the customer, it is apparent that someone other than the customer has accessed the customer's covered account: 
1.  Change any account numbers, passwords, security codes, or other security devices that permit access to an account; or 
2.  Close the account. 
c.  Cease attempts to collect additional charges from the customer and decline to sell the customer's account to a debt collector in the event that the customer's account has been accessed without authorization and such access has caused additional charges to accrue; 
d.  Notify a debt collector within 24 business hours of the discovery of likely or probable identity theft relating to a customer account that has been sold to such debt collector in the event that a customer's account has been sold to a debt collector prior to the discovery of the likelihood or probability of identity theft relating to such account; 
e.  Notify law enforcement, in the event that someone other than the customer has accessed the customer's account causing additional charges to accrue or accessing personal identifying information; or 
f.  Take other appropriate action to prevent or mitigate identity theft. 
(2)  In the event that any city employee responsible for or involved in opening a new covered account becomes aware of red flags indicating possible identity theft with respect an application for a new account, such employee shall use his or her discretion to determine whether such red flag or combination of red flags suggests a threat of identity theft. If, in his or her discretion, such employee determines that identity theft or attempted identity theft is likely or probable, such employee shall immediately report such red flags to the city administrator. If, in his or her discretion, such employee deems that identity theft is unlikely or that reliable information is available to reconcile red flags, the employee shall convey this information to the city administrator, who may in his or her discretion determine that no further action is necessary. If the city administrator in his or her discretion determines that further action is necessary, a city employee shall perform one or more of the following responses, as determined to be appropriate by the city administrator: 
a.  Request additional identifying information from the applicant; 
b.  Deny the application for the new account; 
c.  Notify law enforcement of possible identity theft; or 
d.  Take other appropriate action to prevent or mitigate identity theft. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § A, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-10. - Updating the program. 
The city council shall annually review and, as deemed necessary by the council, update the identity theft prevention program along with any relevant red flags in order to reflect changes in risks to customers or to the safety and soundness of the city and its covered accounts from identity theft. In so doing, the city council shall consider the following factors and exercise its discretion in amending the program: 
(1)  The city's experiences with identity theft; 
(2)  Updates in methods of identity theft; 
(3)  Updates in customary methods used to detect, prevent, and mitigate identity theft; 
(4)  Updates in the types of accounts that the city offers or maintains; and 
(5)  Updates in service provider arrangements. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § A, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-11. - Program administration. 
The city administrator is responsible for oversight of the program and for program implementation. The city administrator is responsible for reviewing reports prepared by staff regarding compliance with red flag requirements and with recommending material changes to the program, as necessary in the opinion of the city administrator, to address changing identity theft risks and to identify new or discontinued types of covered accounts. Any recommended material changes to the program shall be submitted to the city council for consideration by the council. 
(1)  The city administrator will report to the mayor and the city council at least annually, on compliance with the red flag requirements. The report will address material matters related to the program and evaluate issues such as: 
a.  The effectiveness of the policies and procedures of city in addressing the risk of identity theft in connection with the opening of covered accounts and with respect to existing covered accounts; 
b.  Service provider arrangements; 
c.  Significant incidents involving identity theft and management's response; and 
d.  Recommendations for material changes to the program. 
(2)  the city administrator is responsible for providing training to all employees responsible for or involved in opening a new covered account, restoring an existing covered account or accepting payment for a covered account with respect to the implementation and requirements of the identity theft prevention program. The city administrator shall exercise his or her discretion in determining the amount and substance of training necessary. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § A, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-12. - Outside service providers. 
In the event that the city engages a service provider to perform an activity in connection with one or more covered accounts the city administrator shall exercise his or her discretion in reviewing such arrangements in order to ensure, to the best of his or her ability, that the service provider's activities are conducted in accordance with policies and procedures, agreed upon by contract, that are designed to detect any red flags that may arise in the performance of the service provider's activities and take appropriate steps to prevent or mitigate identity theft. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § A, 10-21-08) 
Secs. 49-13—49-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TREATMENT OF ADDRESS DISCREPANCIES 

Sec. 49-21. - Short title. 
[This article shall be known as] treatment of address discrepancies. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § B, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-22. - Purpose. 
Pursuant to 16 CFR § 681.1, the purpose of this article is to establish a process by which the city will be able to form a reasonable belief that a consumer report relates to the consumer about whom it has requested a consumer credit report when the city has received a notice of address discrepancy. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § B, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-23. - Definitions. 
For purposes of this article, the following definitions apply: 
City means City of Blackshear. 
Notice of address discrepancy means a notice sent to a user by a consumer reporting agency pursuant to 15 U.S.C. § 1681(c)(h)(1), that informs the user of a substantial difference between the address for the consumer that the user provided to request the consumer report and the address(es) in the agency's file for the consumer. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § B, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-24. - Policy. 
In the event that the city receives a notice of address discrepancy, the city employee responsible for verifying consumer addresses for the purpose of providing the municipal service or account sought by the consumer shall perform one or more of the following activities, as determined to be appropriate by such employee: 
(1)  Compare the information in the consumer report with: 
a.  Information the city obtains and uses to verify a consumer's identity in accordance with the requirements of the customer information program rules implementing 31 U.S.C. § 5318(l); 
b.  Information the city maintains in its own records, such as applications for service, change of address notices, other customer account records or tax records; or 
c.  Information the city obtains from third-party sources that are deemed reliable by the relevant city employee; or 
(2)  Verify the information in the consumer report with the consumer. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § B, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-25. - Furnishing consumer's address to consumer reporting agency. 
(1)  In the event that the city reasonably confirms that an address provided by a consumer to the city is accurate, the city is required to provide such address to the consumer reporting agency from which the city received a notice of address discrepancy with respect to such consumer. This information is required to be provided to the consumer reporting agency when: 
a.  The city is able to form a reasonable belief that the consumer report relates to the consumer about whom the city requested the report; 
b.  The city establishes a continuing relation with the consumer; and 
c.  The city regularly and in the ordinary course of business provides information to the consumer reporting agency from which it received the notice of address discrepancy. 
(2)  Such information shall be provided to the consumer reporting agency as part of the information regularly provided by the city to such agency for the reporting period in which the city establishes a relationship with the customer. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § B, 10-21-08) 
Sec. 49-26. - Methods of confirming consumer addresses. 
The city employee charged with confirming consumer addresses may, in his or her discretion, confirm the accuracy of an address through one or more of the following methods: 
(1)  Verifying the address with the consumer; 
(2)  Reviewing the city's records to verify the consumer's address; 
(3)  Verifying the address through third-party sources; or 
(4)  Using other reasonable processes. 
(Ord. No. 2008-05, § B, 10-21-08) 
Chapter 50 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6; animals, ch. 10; courts, ch. 30; parks and recreation, ch. 54; traffic and vehicles, ch. 70. 
State Law reference— Criminal Code of Georgia, O.C.G.A. § 16-1-1 et seq.; limitation on home rule powers of municipal corporations with respect to duplication of state criminal offenses, O.C.G.A. § 36-35-6(a)(2). 

Sec. 50-1. - Disorderly conduct. 
It shall be unlawful for any person within the corporate limits of the city to violate any of the following subsections: 
(1)  Any person who shall act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, where any person is reasonably placed in fear of safety of his life, limb, or health; 
(2)  Any person who shall act in a violent or tumultuous manner toward another, where property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or damaged; 
(3)  Any person who shall endanger lawful pursuits of another by acts of violence, angry threats, and abusive conduct; 
(4)  Any person who shall cause, provoke, or engage in any fight, brawl, or riotous conduct so as to endanger the life, limb, health, or property of another; 
(5)  Any person who shall assemble or congregate with another for the purpose of causing, provoking, or engaging in any fight or brawl; 
(6)  Any person who shall be found jostling or roughly crowding or pushing any person in any public place; 
(7)  Any person who shall solicit funds in crowds for unlawful purposes; 
(8)  Any person who shall assemble or congregate with another for the purpose of or with the intent to engage in gaming; 
(9)  Any person who shall frequent any public place with intent to obtain money from another by an illegal and fraudulent scheme, trick, artifice, or device; 
(10)  Any person who assembles with another for the purpose of engaging in any fraudulent scheme, device, or trick to obtain any valuable thing in any place or from any person in the town, or who shall aid or abet such person; 
(11)  Any person who utters, while in a state of anger, in the presence of another, any lewd or obscene words or epithets; 
(12)  Any person who frequents any establishment where gaming or the illegal sale or possession of alcoholic beverages or narcotics or dangerous drugs is allowed or tolerated; 
(13)  Any person who shall act in such a manner as to cause another person to reasonably be in fear of bodily harm or injury; 
(14)  Any person who shall use "fighting words" directed towards any person who becomes outraged and thus creates turmoil; 
(15)  Any person who shall assemble or congregate with another for the purpose of doing bodily harm to another; 
(16)  Any person who shall, by acts of violence, interfere with another's pursuit of a lawful occupation; 
(17)  Any person who shall congregate with another in or on any public way, so as to halt the flow of vehicular or pedestrian traffic, and refuses to clear any public way when ordered to do so; 
(18)  Any person who recklessly or knowingly commits any act which may be reasonably expected to prevent or disrupt any meeting or any public or quasi-public agency or religious worship within the city. 
Any person who shall violate any subsection of this section may be charged with the offense of "disorderly conduct", and on conviction thereof, shall be found guilty of disorderly conduct and shall be punished pursuant to section 1-12 of this Code. 
(Code 1987, § 14-1; Ord. No. 2009-13, art. I, 11-10-09) 
Sec. 50-2. - Drinking in public. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to consume any alcoholic beverage in or upon any street, alley, sidewalk, or other public way or place in the city, or within any public building. 
(Code 1987, § 3-4) 
Sec. 50-3. - Loitering or prowling. 
(a)  A person commits the offense of loitering or prowling when he is in a place at a time or in a manner not usual for law-abiding individuals under circumstances that warrant a justifiable and reasonable alarm or immediate concern for the safety of persons or property in the vicinity. 
(b)  Among the circumstances which may be considered in determining whether alarm is warranted is the fact that the person takes flight upon the appearance of a law enforcement officer, refuses to identify himself, or manifestly endeavors to conceal himself or any object. Unless flight by the person or other circumstances make it impracticable, a law enforcement officer shall, prior to any arrest for an offense under this section, afford the person an opportunity to dispel any alarm or immediate concern which would otherwise be warranted by requesting the person to identify himself and explain his presence and conduct. No person shall be convicted of an offense under this section if the law enforcement officer failed to comply with the foregoing procedure or if it appears at trial that the explanation given by the person was true and would have dispelled the alarm or immediate concern. 
(c)  A person committing the offense of loitering or prowling shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-12. 
(Code 1987, § 14-2) 
State Law reference— Loitering or prowling, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-36. 
Sec. 50-4. - Presence of minor persons upon public streets between certain hours. 
It shall be unlawful for any person under the age of 18 years to loiter, idle, wander, stroll or operate a vehicle upon the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, public buildings, places of public gathering and assembly, vacant lots or other places within the corporate limits of the city between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 6:00 a.m. of the following day; provided, however, that the provisions of this section do not apply to any person upon an emergency errand or legitimate and legal business. 
(Code 1987, § 14-3) 
Sec. 50-5. - Offenses involving utility services. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority to destroy, damage or tamper with any meter, pipe, conduit, wire, line, post, lamp or other apparatus owned by the city, or by any company engaged in the manufacture or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone, cable television, or other public service within the city. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person intentionally and without authority to prevent a meter from properly registering the quantity of such service supplied, or in any way to interfere with the proper action of the city, or of a company engaged, in the manufacture or sale of electricity, gas, water, telephone, cable television or other public service, or intentionally to divert any of the services of the city or such company, or otherwise intentionally and without authority to use or cause to be used, without the consent of the city or such company, any service manufactured, sold or distributed by the city or such company. 
(c)  No person shall knowingly receive the benefit of acts of diversion of or tampering with electricity, gas, water, telephone, cable television or other public service without the proper charge. 
(d)  Proof that any of the acts hereinbefore specified in this action was done on premises in possession of an accused, or that the accused received the benefit of any such act, shall be prima facie evidence that the accused committed such act or aided and abetted in the commission thereof. 
(Code 1987, § 14-4) 
State Law reference— Damaging, injuring or interfering with utilities, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-25. 
Sec. 50-6. - Switchboxes controlling traffic lights. 
It shall be unlawful for anyone to tamper with or damage any switchbox for control of traffic lights. 
(Code 1987, § 14-5) 
Sec. 50-7. - Discharging firearms, airguns, etc. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person in the city to discharge any gun, pistol, or other firearm within 300 yards of any street, alley or building, or at any point upon the land of another person without the express consent of the owner or occupant thereof; or to discharge at any time, any airgun, BB gun or toy gun which projects lead or any other missile. 
(b)  This section shall not be construed to prohibit any officer of the law from discharging a firearm in the performance of officer's duty; nor any citizen from discharging a firearm when lawfully defending person or property. 
(Code 1987, § 14-6) 
Sec. 50-8. - Report of treatment of wounds. 
All physicians and all hospital superintendents in the city are hereby required to report to the police department of the city all patients treated by physicians or diagnosed or known to be suffering from wounds inflicted by a dangerous or deadly weapon of any kind. Such report may be made in writing or by telephone, giving the name of the reporting person and the patient and any other pertinent date requested by the police department. All reports shall be made within 24 hours after treatment by a physician or after admission to the hospital. 
(Code 1987, § 14-7) 
Sec. 50-9. - Throwing of missiles. 
It shall be unlawful for any person in the city to throw any stone, rock, or other missile upon or at any vehicle, building, tree, or other public or private property, or upon or at any person in any public or private way or place. 
(Code 1987, § 14-8) 
Sec. 50-10. - Ballplaying. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to play ball by throwing, catching, pitching, or batting a ball on any public street, alley or sidewalk of the city. 
(Code 1987, § 14-9) 
Sec. 50-11. - Smoking in city buildings prohibited. 
(a)  Smoking is hereby prohibited in all of the buildings owned or occupied by the city. 
(b)  The mayor of the city shall proceed immediately to post each site indicating that smoking is prohibited and that violation of this section shall subject the violator to prosecution. 
(c)  Any city police officer, or other law enforcement officer, shall be authorized to issue citations to violators of any provision of this section. Such citation shall summon the violator to appear before the municipal court, shall identify the offense with which the accused is charged, shall have an identifying number by which it shall be filed with the court, shall indicate the identity of the accused and the date of service, and shall be signed by the officer who completes and services it. 
(d)  Any person violating this section, or any provision hereof upon conviction, shall be punished as follows: 
First offense, warning 
Second offense, fine of $10.00 
Third offense, fine of $25.00 
All subsequent offenses, $25.00 
(1)  The judge of the municipal court shall have the authority and discretion to suspend or probate any part of the sentence. Further, the judge of the municipal court shall permit the sentenced party to perform community service at the rate of $5.00 per hour. The performance of such community service shall be in compliance with such conditions as the municipal judge shall order. 
(2)  The person accused of violating this section shall be arrested and required to post bond for his future appearance in an amount as set by order of the municipal judge. 
(3)  Violation of this section shall be tried upon citation as described in subsection (c) of this section and may be tried with a prosecuting attorney. The city attorney shall serve as prosecuting attorney. 
(4)  Each violation of this section shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1987, § 14-11; Ord. of 2-11-92, §§ I—V) 
State Law reference— Smoking in public places, O.C.G.A. § 16-12-2. 
Sec. 50-12. - Begging. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to beg or solicit money or aid in his own behalf in any place of business, residence (excepting only the persons' personal residence) or upon any of the streets and roads of the city. 
(b)  Any person violating any provision of this section shall be punished by a fine for the first offense of not less than $25.00. For the second offense, the fine shall be now less than $50.00. If a third offense is committed within one year of conviction of a second offense, the minimum fine shall be $100.00. 
(Ord. No. 2009-02, 1-20-09) 
Chapter 54 - PARKS AND RECREATION[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6; fire prevention and protection, ch. 38; health and sanitation, ch. 46; offenses and miscellaneous provisions, ch. 50; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66; traffic and vehicles, ch. 70. 
State Law reference— State parks, O.C.G.A. § 12-3-1 et seq.; authority of municipality to construct and operate parks, swimming pools, golf courses, recreation grounds and buildings used for sports, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-3; establishment of recreation systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-1 et seq.; recreation boards, O.C.G.A. § 36-64-5; Georgia state games commission, O.C.G.A. § 50-12-40 et seq.; power to provide parks, recreation areas, programs and facilities, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(5). 

Sec. 54-1. - Development of municipal recreation programs. 
The authority to develop programs of recreational activities and services designed to meet the leisure time interest and needs of all municipal citizens is hereby granted to and vested in the park and recreation board, which board shall have the power to maintain and equip parks, playgrounds, recreation centers, and the buildings associated therewith, and to develop, maintain, and operate all types of recreation facilities. 
(Code 1987, § 15-1) 
Sec. 54-2. - Use of grounds and facilities in general. 
Each person using the public parks and grounds shall clean up all debris, extinguish all fires when such fires are permitted, and leave the premises in good order and the facilities in a neat and sanitary condition. 
(Code 1987, § 15-2) 
Sec. 54-3. - Prohibited acts. 
It shall be unlawful for any person using public parks, grounds, or facilities to either perform or permit to be performed any of the following acts: 
(1)  Willfully mark, deface, disfigure, damage, tamper with, or displace or remove, any buildings; bridges; tables; benches; fireplaces; railings; paving or paving material; waterlines or other public utilities or parts or appurtenances thereof; signs, notices, or placards, whether temporary or permanent; monuments; stakes, posts, or other boundary markers; or other structures or equipment, facilities or park property or appurtenances whatsoever, either real or personal. 
(2)  Throw, discharge, or otherwise place or cause to be placed in the waters of any fountain, pond, lake, stream, bay, or other body of water in or adjacent to any park or any tributary, stream, storm sewer, or drain flowing into such waters, any substance, matter or thing, liquid or solid, which will or may result in the pollution of such waters. 
(3)  Damage, cut, carve, transplant, or remove any tree or plant or any part thereof. 
(4)  Hunt, molest, harm, frighten, kill, trap, chase, tease, shoot, or throw missiles at any animal, reptile, or bird; or remove or have in one's possession the young of any wild animal, or the eggs, nest, or young of any wild bird. 
(5)  Bring in or dump, deposit, or leave any bottles, broken glass, ashes, paper, boxes, cans, dirt, rubbish, waste, garbage, refuse, or other trash. No such refuse or trash shall be placed in any waters in or contiguous to any park, or left anywhere on the grounds thereof, but shall be placed in the proper receptacles where such receptacles are provided; and where receptacles are not so provided, all such rubbish or waste shall be carried away from the park by the person responsible for the presence of same, and properly disposed of elsewhere. 
(6)  Disturb the peace, or use any profane or obscene language. 
(7)  Endanger the safety of any person by any conduct or act. 
(8)  Commit any assault or battery, or engage in fighting. 
(9)  Carry, possess, or drink any alcoholic beverage in the park. 
(10)  Violate any rule for the use of the park, made or approved by the park and recreation board or by the council. 
(11)  Prevent any person from using any park, or any of its facilities, or interfere with such use in compliance with this chapter and with the rules applicable to such use. 
(12)  Swim, bathe, or wade in any waters or waterways in or adjacent to any park, except in such waters and at such places as are provided therefor, and in compliance with such regulations as are herein set forth or may be hereafter adopted. 
(13)  Dress or undress on any beach, or in any vehicle, toilet, or other place, except in such bathing houses or structures as may be provided for that purpose. 
(Code 1987, § 15-3) 
Sec. 54-4. - Hours of operation. 
(a)  The public parks shall be open daily to the public during the hours of 8:00 a.m. to 11:00 p.m. It shall be unlawful for any person other than city personnel conducting city business therein to occupy or be present in such parks during any other hours. 
(b)  Any section or part of a park, or an entire park, may be declared closed to the public by the superintendent of public works at any time for any interval of time, either temporarily or at regular or stated intervals. 
(Code 1987, § 15-4) 
Sec. 54-5. - Group activity. 
When members of any group, association, or organization desire to use any park facilities for a particular purpose, such as picnics, parties, or theatrical or other entertainment performances, such members will send a representative of such group, association, or organization to first obtain approval from the director of recreation. 
(Code 1987, § 15-5) 
Sec. 54-6. - Games. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to take part in or abet the playing of any game involving thrown or otherwise propelled objects such as balls, stones, arrows, javelins, or model airplanes except in areas set apart for such forms of recreation. The playing of rough or potentially dangerous games such as football, baseball, and soccer is prohibited except on the fields, courts, or areas provided therefor. 
(Code 1987, § 15-6) 
Sec. 54-7. - Camping. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to set up tents, shacks, or any other temporary shelter for the purpose of overnight camping, or for any person to leave in a park after closing hours any movable structure or special vehicle to be used, or that could be used, for such purpose, such as a house trailer, camp trailer, camp wagon, or the like. 
(Code 1987, § 15-7) 
Sec. 54-8. - Fires. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to build or attempt to build a fire except in such areas and under such regulations as may be designated by the superintendent of public works. No person shall drop, throw, or otherwise scatter lighted matches, burning cigarettes, or cigars, tobacco paper, or other inflammable material within any park area or on any highway, road, or street abutting or contiguous thereto. 
(Code 1987, § 15-8) 
Sec. 54-9. - Animals. 
It shall be unlawful to bring any dangerous animal into any park. It shall be unlawful to permit any dog to be in any park unless such dog is on a leash not more than five feet long. 
(Code 1987, § 15-9) 
Sec. 54-10. - Motor vehicles. 
It shall be unlawful to drive or park any motor vehicle except on a street, driveway, or parking lot in any park; or to park, or leave any such vehicle in any place other than one established for public parking. 
(Code 1987, § 15-10) 
Sec. 54-11. - Sales. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to vend, sell, peddle, or offer for sale any commodity or article within any park, except on special occasions as approved by the council. 
(Code 1987, § 15-11) 
Sec. 54-12. - Alcoholic beverages. 
It shall be unlawful for any person within any park to have in such person's possession, custody, or control any alcoholic beverage of any kind whatsoever. 
(Code 1987, § 15-12) 
Sec. 54-13. - Signs. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to paste, glue, tack, or otherwise post any sign, placard, advertisement, or inscription whatever, or for any person to erect or cause to be erected any sign whatever on any public land or highway or road adjacent to a park, except that these provisions shall not apply to any properly authorized government official in pursuit of any official duty. 
(Code 1987, § 15-13) 
Chapter 58 - SIGNS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6; buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; businesses, ch. 18; streets, sidewalks and other public places, ch. 66. 
State Law reference— Prohibited placement of campaign posters, signs and advertisements, O.C.G.A. § 21-1-1; signs used by retail distilled spirits dealers; signs advertising Georgia lottery, O.C.G.A. § 3-4-3; control of signs and signals, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-50 et seq.; unlawful placement of signs within right-of-way of public road, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-51; outdoor advertising near state highways, O.C.G.A. § 32-6-70 et seq. 

Sec. 58-1. - General provisions. 
(a)  All types of signs, except outdoor advertising signs, shall be allowed in all zoning districts without a permit. 
(b)  All outdoor advertising signs shall be subject to the same yard and height limitations imposed upon other buildings or structures in the use district in which such sign is located, except as otherwise provided herein. 
(c)  For the purpose of computing sign area, only one side of a "V-Type" or double-faced outdoor advertising sign shall be considered. 
(d)  Rooftop outdoor advertising signs or sign structures shall not extend more than 30 feet above the roof line. Rooftop outdoor advertising signs or sign structures shall not extend beyond or overhang any exterior wall of the building upon which secured. 
(e)  No outdoor advertising sign or sign structure shall be placed upon any street, sidewalk, or highway right-of-way. All signs must have a setback of three feet from property line. 
(f)  No outdoor advertising sign shall be erected, relocated or maintained so as to prevent free ingress to or egress from any door, window or fire escape. 
(g)  No portion of any outdoor advertising sign shall be less than ten feet above the level of a sidewalk or other pedestrian thoroughfare, nor be less than 16 feet above the level of a public driveway, alley or street. 
(h)  Any sign not particularly designated above shall be subject to the control and supervision of the city council. 
(Code 1987, § 5-70) 
Sec. 58-2. - Outdoor advertising signs as permitted uses. 
(a)  Residential districts. No outdoor advertising signs are permitted in residential districts in the city. 
(b)  Commercial districts. One outdoor advertising sign for each lot of 100 feet or less or lot frontage with one additional sign for each additional 100 feet or less of lot frontage under single ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this chapter was derived, and provided such sign shall not exceed 800 square feet in area per structure facing. Where two signs, each not exceeding 600 square feet in area per structure facing are supported by the same sign structure, one above the other, they shall be considered as a single outdoor advertising sign. 
(c)  Wholesale and industrial districts. One outdoor advertising sign for each lot of 75 feet or less of lot frontage with one additional sign for each additional 75 feet or less of lot frontage under single ownership at the time of the passage of the ordinance from which this chapter was derived, and provided such sign shall not exceed 800 square feet in area per structure facing. Where signs, each not exceeding 600 feet in area per structure facing are supported by the same sign structure, one above the other, they shall be considered as a single outdoor advertising sign. 
(d)  Mobile business signs. Class 8 mobile business signs, single- or double-faced provided that they: 
(1)  Shall have a maximum size of 15 feet for each side; 
(2)  There is only one sign for each zoning lot on which the sign is located; 
(3)  Shall be set back at least five feet from property line with flashing light; bulbs not to exceed 60 watt, or three feet setback without flashing lights; 
(4)  All electrical hook-ups shall be approved by city building inspector. 
(Code 1987, § 5-71) 
Sec. 58-3. - Signs prohibited in all districts. 
The following signs are prohibited in all use districts: 
(1)  Any sign erected or painted upon a sloping roof, fence, tree, stand-pipe, fire escape or utility pole. 
(2)  Any sign which uses the word "Stop" or "Danger" prominently displayed or which is a copy or imitation of an official traffic control sign. 
(Code 1987, § 5-72) 
Sec. 58-4. - Maintenance and removal of outdoor advertising signs. 
(a)  All outdoor advertising signs and sign structures shall be kept in repair and in proper state preservation. All unsafe signs must adhere to the provisions of the city building code. 
(b)  Outdoor advertising signs which are no longer functional or are abandoned, shall be removed, or relocated, at the owner's expense, in compliance with the provisions of this chapter within 30 days following malfunction. 
(c)  Any legally established nonconforming outdoor advertising signs or sign structure shall be permitted without alteration in size or location, provided that the requirements of this chapter are adhered to and provided that nothing herein shall prevent maintenance, repairing or posting of legally established nonconforming signs. 
(d)  Upon destruction, partial or complete, of an outdoor advertising sign, the owner thereof shall have the right to reconstruct, rebuild, renovate, or repair such sign substantially to the same condition as before such destruction, provided the provisions of this chapter are adhered to. 
(Code 1987, § 5-73) 
Sec. 58-5. - Temporary signs. 
(a)  A temporary sign is a sign or sign structure which is not constructed for permanent use and advertises an event or activity occurring at a specific time or period or time. Examples of temporary signs are political advertisements, open house advertisements, and yard sale advertisements. Temporary signs do not include portable signs which are constructed for permanent use. 
(b)  A political advertisement shall not be permitted for a period longer than 60 days, except that when a candidate wins a primary election, such political advertisement may remain until the general election, but in no case shall the additional time be greater than 90 days. 
(c)  A temporary sign shall be removed by the owner or owner's designee within three days after the final date of the event or activity to which the sign makes reference. Failure of owner or owner's designee to remove a temporary sign within the time period prescribed in this Code section may result in the collection and destruction of the temporary sign by a representative of the city. Any cost associated with such removal and destruction may be administratively assessed by the city against the owner of the sign. 
(d)  All vehicular signs shall adhere to the requirements set forth herein except for those signs not exceeding 40 square feet and attached to vehicles which are used primarily for other purposes than displaying an outdoor advertising sign. 
(e)  Signs which display general advertisements or commercial promotions are prohibited. 
(Code 1987, § 5-74; Ord. No. 2013-03, § 1, 4-9-13) 
Chapter 62 - SOLID WASTE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— The city is a participating party in the Tri-County Solid Waste Management Plan dated October 1992. This plan was prepared to assist the counties of Bacon, Pierce and Ware and their municipalities in complying with the requirements of the Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq. An official copy of the plan is on file in the office of the city clerk. 
Cross reference— Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; environment, ch. 34; health and sanitation, ch. 46; utilities, ch. 74. 
State Law reference— Georgia Comprehensive Solid Waste Management Act, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-20 et seq.; local, multijurisdictional and regional solid waste plans, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-31.1; scrap tire disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.1; yard trimmings disposal restrictions, O.C.G.A. § 12-8-40.2; litter Control Law, O.C.G.A. § 16-7-40 et seq.; authorization to provide garbage and solid waste collection and disposal, Ga. Const. art. IX, § II, ¶ III(a)(2); transporting garbage or waste across state or county boundaries without permission, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-16; littering highways, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-249; transportation of biomedical waste, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-253.1; solid waste management education program; establishment of Georgia Clean and Beautiful Advisory Committee and Interagency Council on Solid Waste Management, O.C.G.A. § 50-8-7.3. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 62-1—62-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL 

Sec. 62-31. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Collection means the work of collecting or transporting solid waste from industries, offices, retail outlets, businesses, institutions, or similar locations, or from residential dwellings; provided, however, that this definition shall not include an individual collecting or transporting waste from such person's single-family dwelling unit. 
Disposal facility means any facility or location where any treatment, utilization, processing or disposition of solid waste occurs. 
Disposal operation means the performance of solid waste disposal, including administration, personnel, land, equipment, design, and other elements necessary or used in the work of solid waste disposal. 
Disposal site means the location or land area where the final disposition of solid waste occurs. 
Garbage means putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking, and consumption of food. 
Hazardous waste means solid or liquid waste material resulting from the manufacture or use of pesticides and drugs (other than normal household use); pathological wastes; highly flammable or explosive wastes; toxic wastes; sewage sludges; and other waste material determined to be a likely hazard to the public health, safety or environment, except radioactive waste materials as provided for in rules of the Georgia Department of Human Resources, Chapter 270-5-20, entitled "Radioactive Materials." 
Industrial waste means waste materials generated in industrial operations. 
Open dump means a disposal site at which solid waste from one or more sources is consolidated and left to decompose, burn, or to otherwise create environmental pollution or nuisance. 
Putrescible wastes means wastes that are capable of being decomposed by microorganisms, including kitchen wastes, manure, offal, hatchery and poultry wastes, and garbage. 
Reclamation means a controlled method of sorting and storing solid wastes for future use in accordance with an approved plan. 
Refuse means all putrescible and nonputrescible solid wastes (except body wastes), including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, abandoned automobiles, and solid commercial and industrial wastes. 
Rubbish means nonputrescible solid wastes (excluding ashes), consisting of both combustible and noncombustible wastes, wood, glass, bedding, crockery, and similar materials. 
Sanitary landfilling means a method of disposing of putrescible waste or hazardous waste on land by placing an earth cover thereon. 
Scavenge means uncontrolled picking from discarded waste materials. 
Solid waste means putrescible and nonputrescible wastes, except body wastes, including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street refuse, dead animals, sewage sludges, animal manures, industrial wastes, residue from incineration, food-processing wastes, construction wastes, hazardous wastes, and any other waste material in a solid or semi-solid state not otherwise defined in this article. 
Solid waste handling means the storage, collection, transportation, treatment, utilization, processing, or disposing of solid wastes, or any combination thereof. 
Storm debris means waste generated by a natural disaster i.e., hurricane, tropical storm, tornado etc. 
Transfer station means a facility used to transfer solid wastes from one transportation vehicle to another for transportation to a disposal facility. 
Yard waste means leaves, pine straw, limbs, grass or cuttings from bushes. 
(Code 1987, § 12-110; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 62-32. - Purpose. 
The purpose of the rules and regulations contained in this article is to provide for the protection of the public health by prescribing the manner of storage, collection, transportation, and disposal of residential and industrial waste, rubbish, garbage, and refuse. 
(Code 1987, § 12-111; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-33. - Enforcement. 
(a)  In general. The superintendent of public works shall be responsible for the administration and enforcement of this article. In the exercise of such solid waste management duties, the superintendent shall: 
(1)  Supervise the collection of solid waste, including the operation and maintenance of equipment and the supervision of personnel; 
(2)  Establish collection schedules in accordance with the provisions of this article; 
(3)  Supervise the operation and maintenance disposal sites or facilities; and 
(4)  Inspect and regulate the operations of private collectors and private transportation and disposal systems to ensure that such operations are in compliance with the provisions of this article. 
(b)  Limitations of authority. All regulatory actions of the superintendent of public works shall be subject to the review of the council. 
(c)  Appeal. Any person aggrieved by a requirement of, or a fee charged by, the superintendent of public works shall have the right to appeal to the council, which body may upon hearing, confirm, modify, or revoke such requirement or fee. 
(Code 1987, § 12-112; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-34. - Precollection. 
(a)  In general. No person shall keep or store solid waste outside of any residence or building within the city, except in proper containers for collection or otherwise prepared, as set forth herein or under the express prior approval of public works. Any unauthorized accumulation of solid waste is hereby declared a nuisance and is prohibited. The superintendent of public works by written notice shall notify the owner or occupant of any premises with such solid waste accumulation to remove same. Failure to remove such accumulation within 14 days of the date of such written notice to do so shall be deemed a violation of these regulations and subject to penalties set forth in this Code. A separate violation shall be deemed committed each day during or upon which such unlawful accumulation continues. 
(b)  Containers. All residential and some small commercial customers will utilize a 96-gallon roll-out container. These containers will be provided to every residence and some small commercial customers on a one-time basis. If a container is removed from the residential or small commercial location the replacement container will be paid for by the occupant or owner of the residential or commercial location. 
(c)  Preparation. 
(1)  Garbage and rubbish shall be drained of excess liquids before being placed for collection. 
(2)  All rubbish shall be placed at the curbside or alleyway for collection, do not place in roadway. 
(3)  Roll-out containers shall be placed at the curbside, or alleyway for collection, do not place in roadway. 
(4)  Yard waste shall be placed at the curbside or alleyway for collection not in roadway. Limbs or cuttings when placed in bundles shall not exceed 35 pounds gross weight per bundle and shall not be over four feet in length and no more than 12 inches in diameter. 
(5)  Trees, large bushes or shrubbery that are trimmed by anyone other than a resident where left for pickup or by commercial trimmers or tree surgeons, are not to be picked up by the city. All persons other than residents trimming or cutting trees, large bushes or shrubbery shall be responsible for disposing of the residue of trees, bushes or shrubbery that are trimmed. 
(6)  Appliances, furniture, and/or white goods (stoves, dishwashers, washers and dryers, etc.) shall not be placed on the curb until the resident has called for a special pickup. Failure to call and request a special pickup shall result in a $25.00 fee for disposal without prior notice. Property owners and/or property management companies that serve dispossessory notice on residents will be responsible for calling for a special pickup the week of the dispossession is to be served on the resident. Failure to comply will result in a fine of $50.00 and a charge for disposal of not less than $75.00 for each pickup when done by the city. 
(d)  Rubbish. Rubbish shall not be placed on the curb until the resident has called for a special pickup. Failure to call and request a special pickup shall result in a $25.00 fee for disposal. The city will provide roll-off dumpsters once per quarter that will allow residents to dispose of rubbish. The actual dates and locations will be published in the legal organ, as well as advertised on the city website. 
(e)  Scavenging. No person other than the owner thereof, or an agent or employee of the city, or any employee of a person holding a contract with the city for collection of solid waste, shall interfere with any container placed for the purpose of storage of solid waste pending collection, or remove or take any of the contents thereof, or remove any such container from the location where same shall have been placed by the owner thereof, unless permission to do so has been granted by the city. 
(Code 1987, § 12-113; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-35. - Collection. 
(a)  Frequency. Garbage and yard waste shall be collected from residential premises weekly. 
(b)  Limitations. Industrial waste or waste from construction, demolition, landscaping, or processing operations will not be collected, transported or disposed of by public facilities, but such waste collection, transportation, and disposal shall be by the owners or generators of such waste. It shall be a violation of these regulations to place or to cause to be placed in any container, box or bundle, or otherwise for collection, any hazardous waste of any kind except upon specific prior arrangement with the superintendent of public works. 
(c)  Collection vehicles. Vehicles used for collection and transportation of solid waste shall be kept clean and in good repair. They shall be constructed in such manner that the contents thereof cannot be spilled, leaked or blown from the vehicle. They shall be readily identifiable by letters, not less than three inches high and easily legible, painted on the door of the vehicle cab or in an equally conspicuous place, showing the owner's name, telephone number, state permit number, truck number, and rated load capacity in cubic yards. The rated load capacity shall be specified by the superintendent of public works following such superintendent's measurement of the load-carrying portion of the truck body. 
(d)  Private contractors. The mayor and council may contract with others to engage in the business of collecting, transporting or disposing of solid waste, provided such persons have applied for and obtained an appropriate solid waste permit in accordance with regulations of the Georgia Code Annotated, tit. 12, Conservation and Natural Resources; ch. 8, Waste Management; art. 2, Solid Waste Management; pt. 1, General Provisions; O.C.G.A. § 12-8-24. Permits for solid waste or special solid waste handling, disposal, or thermal treatment technology facility; inspection of solid waste generators. Persons contracting for solid waste collections shall, before engaging in such business, be licensed by the city, shall conform to all regulations providing for safe and sanitary collection and transportation of waste to a point of disposal. 
(Code 1987, § 12-114; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-36. - Disposal. 
(a)  All disposal of house hold garbage and rubbish shall be at disposal sites operated in accordance with state laws and with rules and regulations of the state department of natural resources, and at no other place. 
(b)  Yard waste shall be mulched at the city's mulching operation. Mulching will be completed by the city's mulching contractor. The facility will be operated in accordance with state laws and with rules and regulations of the state department of natural resources, and at no other place. 
(c)  Storm debris (debris generated by hurricane, tropical storm, etc.) may be disposed of by utilizing the city's mulching contractor or by open burning provided a variance permit is obtained from the environmental protection division (EPD). Open burning will only be allowed from qualifying storm events as determined by EPD. 
(Code 1987, § 12-115; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-37. - Frequency of residential pickup. 
Solid waste pickup for residential areas in the city shall be once each week for each household. 
(Ord. of 12-8-92, § 1; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-38. - Rates—Residential. 
Each household shall pay an amount as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges per month for solid waste pickup. 
(Code 1987, § 12-8; Ord. of 12-8-92, § 2; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-39. - Same—Commercial. 
Solid waste pickup and charges for commercial and other business establishments shall be as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges. 
(Code 1987, § 12-8; Ord. of 12-8-92, § 3; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-40. - Same—Billing. 
(a)  Service charges in accordance with the schedule are levied against the occupant of premises served, jointly and severally, but collecting from one shall relieve the other. 
(b)  Charges for solid waste collection and disposal service shall be billed each month in conjunction with the regular water and sewer bill. These charges are due and payable at time the bill is rendered. Payments are due not later than the tenth calendar day of the following month, unless the tenth day shall fall on a Saturday or a Sunday, in which case the bill will be due not later than the close of business on the next business day. Bills are payable at the office of the city treasurer. When such payment has not been made by the 15th day of the month, service shall be discontinued until all arrears, including penalty, have been paid in full. 
(Code 1987, § 12-9; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-41. - Solid waste collection franchises and fees. 
(a)  All residential, commercial, industrial and institutional establishments within the incorporated limits of the City of Blackshear shall utilize the solid waste collection service of a waste services provider granted a solid waste collection franchise by the city pursuant to the requirements of this section. No waste service provider which has failed to comply with the requirements of this section shall haul away or remove for disposal any solid waste from any residential, commercial, industrial, institutional, or other premises within the incorporated limits of the City of Blackshear. 
(b)  Upon approval of the mayor and council the city may enter into an agreement with a solid waste provider granting an exclusive franchise for solid waste collection and disposal services to residential, commercial, industrial and institutional establishments within the incorporated limits of the city. No exclusive franchise for waste services granted by the city shall include collection of construction or demolition waste collected in roll-off containers from residential, commercial, industrial, or other premises, which shall be authorized by the city through non-exclusive franchises as provided herein. Pursuant to authority of the mayor and council, the City of Blackshear has entered into an exclusive franchise agreement for waste collection services with Republic Services of Georgia, Limited Partnership d/b/a Southland Waste Systems, excluding construction and demolition waste collection. 
(c)  A waste services provider having an exclusive franchise agreement with the city pursuant to this section to provide residential, commercial and industrial solid waste collection services inside the incorporated limits of the City of Blackshear shall be required to pay the city an annual franchise fee of $4,000.00. Unless already paid to the city for the current year, said franchise fee shall be paid to the city within 30 days following official adoption of this section, and annually thereafter on or about the same date. For purposes of this section "residential solid waste" means all solid waste generated by residential premises, and "commercial solid waste" means all solid waste generated by or at any commercial business including any governmental premises and public or private institutional premises. 
(d)  Any waste services provider authorized by the city pursuant to this section to perform solid waste services for collection and disposal of construction and demolition waste collected in roll-off containers from premises located within the incorporated limits of the City of Blackshear shall pay the city an annual franchise fee of $1,000.00. Said franchise fee shall be paid to the city within 30 days following the date of official adoption of this section and annually thereafter on or about the same date. "Construction and demolition waste" shall mean solid waste materials generated by the construction, remodeling, repair or demolition of residential, commercial, industrial, or other premises within the incorporated limits of the City of Blackshear. 
(e)  As used herein a "waste services provider" means a person engaged in the collection and disposal of solid waste in return for a fee paid by the waste generator. Nothing in this section is intended to prevent a construction or demolition contractor from hauling construction or demolition waste for disposal in a truck or trailer belonging to the contractor. 
(f)  Any violation of the solid waste collection franchise requirements of this section shall be subject to enforcement by the city as provided in section 62-33 of this chapter. Appropriate actions and proceedings may be taken by law or in equity to prevent, restrain, correct, or abate any violation of this section. 
(Ord. No. 2010-03, § I, 11-9-10; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Sec. 62-42. - Yard debris pickup. 
All customers of the city water and/or sewer department shall be required to pay a monthly fee with the regular monthly utility bill for the collection of yard debris, in order to protect and guard the health, safety and sanitation of the citizens of the city. The monthly charge shall be established by the city council by resolution from time to time. Upon the refusal of any such customer to pay the monthly fee for yard trash, the city may withhold water and or sewer service and/or sewer service and/or terminate such service. 
(Ord. No. 2011-09, § 1, 1-9-12; Ord. No. 2016-07, § 1, 11-10-16) 
Chapter 66 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND OTHER PUBLIC PLACES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Cross reference— Buildings and building regulations, ch. 14; cemeteries, ch. 22; fire prevention and protection, ch. 38; health and sanitation, ch. 46; parks and recreation, ch. 54; signs, ch. 58; utilities, ch. 74. 
State Law reference— Municipal street systems, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-90 et seq.; powers with respect to municipal street system, O.C.G.A. § 32-4-92; grant by municipal corporation of right to obstruct public street prohibited, O.C.G.A. § 36-30-10; power of city to open, close or extend public streets, alleys and sidewalks, O.C.G.A. § 36-34-3; municipal street improvements, O.C.G.A. § 36-39-1 et seq.; executions for collection of municipal assessments for paving streets and laying sewers, O.C.G.A. § 48-5-358. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 66-1. - Street names—Authority of council generally. 
The city council by resolution may change, rename, or name an existing or newly established street within the city at any time, upon recommendation of the planning commission. 
(Code 1987, § 16-1) 
Sec. 66-2. - Same—Naming unnamed streets; changing names to avoid confusion. 
(a)  In case of streets which bear no names the city council shall be empowered to choose names which they feel are appropriate and which are suitable to the residents of such street. 
(b)  In the case of streets which bear a name in common with another street or if the name is similar enough so as to cause confusion, the city council shall be empowered to rename one of the streets. 
(Code 1987, § 16-2) 
Sec. 66-3. - Streets in subdivisions. 
Every subdivision plat submitted to the council for approval shall bear upon its face the proper names of all streets, avenues, and other public ways dedicated to public use within the jurisdiction of the council, which shall first have been checked and approved by the planning commission. 
(Code 1987, § 16-3) 
Sec. 66-4. - Inspections of projections over public streets. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of the building inspector to inspect semi-annually all awnings, sheds, coverings, and other projections extending over the public streets, sidewalks and roads within the corporate limits of the city; and to make a written report of such inspections to the city council. 
(b)  Any awning, shed, covering, and other projection extending over the public streets, sidewalks and roads found to be in a defective or dangerous condition, shall be condemned and shall be immediately reported to the owner of such property and if the owner cannot be found, then to the occupant of such property. 
(c)  If such condemned awning, shed, covering, and other projection extending over the public streets, sidewalks and roads are not repaired and placed in a safe condition within 30 days, it shall be the duty of the building inspector, with the aid and assistance of the police department, to remove such condemned awning, shed, covering and other projection. 
(Code 1987, § 16-4) 
Sec. 66-5. - Permit for construction of paved driveway. 
(a)  An application for a permit to construct paved driveways on city rights-of-way shall be obtained from the city superintendent of public works, and that no such construction shall begin until such permit and pertinent specifications have been provided. 
(b)  The fee for the permit shall be as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges. 
(c)  Driveways constructed on city rights-of-way, which are out of compliance with city specifications, shall be removed at the owner's expense. 
(Code 1987, § 16-5; Ord. of 2-9-93, §§ 1—3) 
Sec. 66-6. - Driveway construction permits. 
(a)  An application for a permit to construct paved driveways on city rights-of-way shall be obtained from the city superintendent of public works. No such construction shall begin until said permit and pertinent specifications have been provided. 
(b)  The fee for the permit shall be as set forth in the schedule of fees and charges. 
(c)  Driveways constructed on city rights-of-way, after the adoption of the ordinance from which this section derives which are out of compliance with city specifications shall be removed at the owner's expense. 
(Ord. of 2-9-93, §§ 1—3) 
Secs. 66-7—66-35. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BUILDING NUMBERING SYSTEM 

Sec. 66-36. - Uniform system established. 
There is hereby established a uniform system for numbering buildings fronting on all streets, avenues, and other public ways in the city. All houses and other buildings shall be numbered in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1987, § 16-20) 
Sec. 66-37. - Base lines; quadrants; diagonal streets. 
(a)  Ware Street to the west of the intersection of Ware Street and U.S. 84 and U.S. 84 to the east of such intersection, shall constitute the base line for numbering buildings along all streets running northerly and southerly and shall be referred to as the east-west base line. Gordon Street, Main Street, (north of College Street) and College Street shall constitute the base line for numbering buildings along all streets running easterly and westerly and shall be referred to as the north-south base line. 
(1)  Each building to the north of the east-west base line and facing a street running in a northerly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location north of such base line. 
(2)  Each building to the south of the east-west base line and facing a street running in a southerly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location south of such base line. 
(3)  Each building to the west of the north-south base line and facing a street running in a westerly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location west of such base line. 
(4)  Each building to the east of the north-south base line and facing a street running in an easterly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location east of such base line. 
(b)  All buildings on diagonal streets shall be numbered the same as buildings on northerly and southerly streets if the diagonal runs more from the north to the south, the same rule shall apply on easterly and westerly streets if the diagonal runs more from east to west. All buildings on diagonal streets having a deviation of exactly 45 degrees shall be numbered the same as buildings on northerly and southerly streets. 
(Code 1987, § 16-21) 
Sec. 66-38. - Commencement and succession of numbers. 
The numbering of buildings on each street shall begin at the base line. All numbers shall be assigned on the basis of one number for each 25 feet except those fronting on the following streets: All buildings fronting on Main Street between U.S. 84 and Park Street or on Taylor Street between Highway Avenue and Central Avenue or on Repparde Street between Highway Avenue and Central Avenue or on Highway Avenue between Main Street and Repparde Street or on Central Avenue between Main Street and Repparde Street shall be assigned numbers on the basis of one number for each 15 feet of frontage. 
(Code 1987, § 16-22) 
Sec. 66-39. - Even-odd number assignment. 
(a)  All buildings on the right side of each street running from the base line bear even numbers. All buildings on the left side of each street running from the base line shall bear odd numbers. 
(b)  All buildings facing streets not extending through the base lines shall be assigned the same relative numbers as if the street extended to the base line. 
(Code 1987, § 16-23) 
Sec. 66-40. - Separate numbers for each entrance. 
Where any building has more than one entrance serving separate occupants, a separate number shall be assigned to each entrance serving a separate occupant. If the building is not located on a lot, parcel or tract which would permit the assignment of one number to each such entrance, letters shall be used, as set forth in section 66-43. 
(Code 1987, § 16-24) 
Sec. 66-41. - Directional prefixes. 
All streets perpendicular to and crossing the east-west base line shall be given a prefix of "north" for the section which lies to the north of the base line and a prefix of "south" for the section which lies to the south of the base line. All streets perpendicular to and crossing the north-south base line shall be given a prefix of "east" for the section which lies to the east of the base line and a prefix of "west" for the section which lies to the west of the base line. 
(Code 1987, § 16-25) 
Sec. 66-42. - Display of numbers. 
(a)  The assigned number shall be displayed within 30 days after receiving the assignment. 
(b)  The numbers shall be conspicuously placed immediately above, on or at the side of the main entrance so that the number can be seen plainly from the street line. 
(c)  Whenever any building is situated such that the main entrance is more than 50 feet from the street line or such entrance is obscured, then the numbers may be placed upon a gatepost, fence, tree, post or other appropriate place so as to be easily discernible from the street. 
(d)  The numerals shall be no less than three inches in height and be made out of a durable and highly visible material. Such numerals shall be placed on a contrasting background. 
(e)  There shall be a penalty incurred of $1.00 for each week which the owner of a building fails to display the assigned number after the assignment of the number. 
(Code 1987, § 16-26) 
Sec. 66-43. - Letter suffixes. 
Where only one number can be assigned to a building, the owner, occupant, or agent of such building who shall desire distinctive numbers for different parts of such building shall use the suffix A, B, C, etc., as may be required. 
(Code 1987, § 16-27) 
Sec. 66-44. - Supplying information of numbers; resolution in case of conflict. 
It shall be the duty of the superintendent of public works to inform any party applying therefor, of the numbers assigned to or embraced within the limits of any lot or property as provided in this article. In case of conflict as to the proper number to be assigned to any building, the superintendent of public works shall determine the number of such building. 
(Code 1987, § 16-28) 
Sec. 66-45. - Obtaining for, and affixing numbers to, new structures. 
(a)  Whenever any house, building, or other structure shall be erected or located in the city, in order to preserve the continuity and uniformity of numbers of the houses, buildings, and other structures, it shall be the duty of the owner to procure the correct numbers as designated from the superintendent of public works for the property and to immediately fasten the numbers so assigned upon such structure or building as provided by this article. 
(b)  No building permit shall be issued for any house, building, or other structure until the owner has procured from the superintendent of public works the official number of the premises. Final approval of any structure shall be withheld by the city building inspector until permanent and proper numbers have been affixed to such structure. 
(Code 1987, § 16-29) 
Secs. 66-46—66-70. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PARADES AND DEMONSTRATIONS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Preventing or disrupting lawful procession, O.C.G.A. § 16-11-34; funeral processions, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-76; operation of motorcycles and motor vehicles in parades, O.C.G.A. § 40-6-7. 

Sec. 66-71. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Assembly means any group of persons who assemble or congregate on any public street, alley or sidewalk in the city for the purpose of displaying, advertising, promoting, exhibiting, advocating or otherwise attracting public attention or for any cause or thing. 
Parade means any group of persons marching or promenading on and along any public street, alley or sidewalk in the city for the purpose of displaying, advertising, promoting, exhibiting, advocating or otherwise attracting public attention to or for any cause or thing. 
(Code 1987, § 17-12(a)) 
Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 66-72. - Approval required. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to parade, assemble or congregate on any public street, alley or sidewalk in the city for any purpose specified in section 66-71, unless the city council shall have previously approved and authorized such parade or assembly. Any person participating in or attending any parade or assembly which has not been authorized and approved by the city council shall be considered as a part of the group constituting such parade or assembly, and upon conviction thereof shall be punished as provided in section 1-12. 
(Code 1987, § 17-12(b)) 
Sec. 66-73. - Application. 
Any person desiring to parade or assemble on any of the public streets, alleys or sidewalks of the city for the purposes in this article shall file an application with the mayor, setting forth the time, place and purpose of such parade or assembly, and obtain a permit before conducting such parade or assembly. 
(Code 1987, § 17-12(c)) 
Secs. 66-74—66-99. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PUBLIC RIGHTS-OF-WAY CLOSING AND/OR ABANDONMENT 

Sec. 66-100. - Intent. 
[The intent of this article is] to establish regulations for the closing and/or abandoning of roads, streets, alleys or public easements in the city; to provide for the harmonious, orderly and progressive development of streets/transportation facilities; to provide for application procedures and data required for consideration; to provide for the enforcement of this article; to provide for fees payable under this article; and for other purposes. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-101. - Application. 
Application for city road, right-of-way or easement closing or abandonment shall be made to the city clerk's office on an application provided by the city. The applicant shall outline the nature of the request and specify the anticipated follow-on use of the road, right-of-way, or easement for which the request is made. The applicant shall provide a plat that shows the right-of-way or easement for which the application is being filed. The plat shall be prepared by a land surveyor registered by the state in accordance with the Georgia Plat Act, O.C.G.A. § 15-6-67. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-102. - Review. 
(a)  The city public works superintendent shall coordinate the review of the request with the community development director, city administrator, city attorney, police chief, fire chief, and utility providers (power, telephone, cable, and gas) and other departments as necessary. All comments made by reviewers shall be written and returned to the city public works superintendent within 30 days of the application filing date. 
(b)  The city public works superintendent shall prepare staff report based upon the written findings that shall be forwarded to the city council. 
(c)  The public works superintendent shall contact the city council clerk to schedule a date for a public hearing with the city council on their next regular meeting date. 
(d)  The city clerk or his/her designee shall advertise a public hearing, giving the nature of the request, the place, date, and time of hearing in the local newspaper at least fifteen days before the hearing. The beginning and ending of the road or easement closing/abandoning shall be posted with the same information by the city clerk. The advertisement shall state the proposed closing/abandonment has "ceased to be used by the public and no longer serves any useful public purpose." 
(e)  The city administrator will place the abandonment request item on the city council official public hearing and meeting agenda as advertised and posted. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-103. - Determination by the city council. 
(a)  If the city council approves the closing and abandonment, the city attorney shall prepare a quitclaim deed and file it for recording with the Pierce County Superior Court if the identity of the grantee for such a deed is clear. The submitted plat may require a revision if the city council placed conditions on the approved abandonment. The applicant shall bear the cost of any required plat modification. The action is final only after the deed is recorded by the city attorney. The original deed (if any) shall be mailed to the applicant(s) by the city clerk. 
(b)  No application for abandonment shall be made, or considered, if any portion of the property sought to be abandoned has been the subject of an abandonment application filed, or considered by the city council, within the immediate preceding one year. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-104. - Fee. 
(a)  Unopened or dirt street or alley. Any request of an unopened, dirt street or alley submitted under the provisions of this article shall be accompanied by a $450.00 non-refundable application fee. The check shall be made payable to the "City of Blackshear." The applicant may withdraw the application or request a postponement of the hearing date once, by submitting a written request to the city administrator, at least seven calendar days, prior to the date set for the public hearing. If a postponement is requested, the applicant will bear the additional administrative charges (advertising and administrative costs) as determined by the city administrator. 
(b)  Paved street. Any request to close and abandon a paved or otherwise improved open street/road under the provisions of this article shall be accompanied by a non-refundable fee of $450.00 and the current department of transportation item mean value of improvements in the right-of-way to reimburse the city for the funds spent on placing improvements in the street. The cost/value shall be determined by the public works superintendent or another office designated by the city council and submitted by written report to the city administrator prior to the public hearing by the city. 
(c)  Cul-de sac required. Any abandonment that results in creating a dead-end road/street shall require the applicant to construct a cul-de-sac at the dead-end road/street. The newly constructed cul-de-sac shall be constructed of the same material as the dead-end road/street. Applicant, in addition to the application fee, shall incur all cost of the cul-de-sac construction, including but not limited to, construction, drainage improvements, right-of-way dedication, etc. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-105. - Definitions. 
The law of the state recognizes three types of roadways: 
(1)  Fee-simple roadway under which complete title is vested in the city. The city actually has a deed to the roadbed and the adjoining right-of-way. If the road is closed, the city has to dispose of the real property at public sale. 
(2)  Easement-type roadway is where the public has no title vested in the city but merely an easement. The adjacent landowners own the ground underneath the road right-of-way. 
(3)  Conditionally owned roadway is where the city owns the road right-of-way, but the right-of-way reverts to the owner if the city ceases using the right-of-way for road purposes. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-106. - Closing and abandoning policies and factors. 
(a)  Policies. In order for a road to be closed, the city council shall determine that all or part of the road has ceased to be used by public so as to no longer serve any substantial useful purpose. This decision is made by the adoption of an ordinance, which is then recorded on the minutes of the city council. Owners of property located on the road shall first be notified of the impending ordinance prior to its passage by the city council. 
(b)  Cul-de-sac. A street/road approved by the city council to be closed/abandoned with a dead-end shall be provided with a cul-de-sac. The cul-de-sac construction should be funded and completed entirely by the applicant before the quit-claim deed(s) are signed by the mayor. The construction shall meet city standards and receive city approval. 
(c)  Considered factors. There are several factors, which should be considered by the city council in deciding whether or not to close a road or street. These factors are hereinafter set out. 
(1)  Source of title. Does the city own fee simple title to the road/street or merely an easement for use by public for road purposes? 
(2)  Present use of road, street or alley. How is the road, street, or alley currently being used? 
a.  General public; 
b.  Limited use by a small group; 
c.  Location of public utilities; or 
d.  Unopened right-of-way. 
(3)  Past history. What use has been made of the road/street in the last 20 years? 
(4)  Potential need for road in the future. What is the potential for development along the proposed closing/abandoning? 
a.  To serve future growth area. 
b.  Transportation plan projects future right-of-way needed. 
c.  Volume to capacity ration shows need to retain street. 
(5)  Cost involved in closing/abandoning or opening road/street. 
a.  Obstructions in or along right-of-way or at ends of road/street. 
b.  Attorneys fees and court costs projected to exceed value of road/street. 
c.  Other. 
(6)  Availability of other means of travel to take place of vehicular traffic using roadway. 
a.  Public transportation. 
b.  Adjoining landowners' assistance. 
c.  Neighborhood. 
d.  Emergency vehicles. 
e.  Garbage pickup. 
f.  Other. 
(7)  Benefit to public in continuing public usage of roadway. 
a.  Serves adjoining landowners. 
b.  Serves neighborhood traffic needs. 
c.  Provides access for emergency vehicles. 
d.  Allows garbage pick-up and other services. 
e.  Other. 
(8)  Benefit to public in closing road. 
a.  Eliminates road grading expense. 
b.  Eliminates traffic movement hazards. 
c.  Allows better land use plan for development of adjoining land. 
d.  Other. 
(9)  Adverse impact to public in closing road. 
a.  Prevents landowner(s) from accessing public road. 
b.  Interrupts comprehensive transportation plan project. 
c.  Interrupts neighborhood to neighborhood transportation connection. 
d.  Other. 
(Ord. of 7-10-07(2), § 1) 
Sec. 66-107. - Enforcement. 
The enforcement of requirements of this article shall be through city attorney or other official designated by the city council.
